Liability for the Sold Item During Khiyar al-Shart: Destruction and Defect
Ruling on liability if item is destroyed in buyer's possession during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation when the sold item is destroyed or becomes permanently defective in the buyer's hand during khiyar al-shart, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
If the item is destroyed in buyer's hand during seller's option, Hanafi: pay value; Shafi'i: pay price.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentaries explains a key application of khiyar al-shart: who bears the loss if the item is destroyed or develops a permanent defect while in the buyer's possession? The answer depends on whether the option belongs to the seller or the buyer, and the nature of the item. We'll unpack the Hanafi position and the disagreement with the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario for destruction
The passage begins with the case where the sold item has the seller's option (khiyar) and is destroyed in the buyer's hand. Determine the ruling according to Hanafi: the buyer pays the value (qimah) on the day of taking possession.
This applies whether the buyer took possession with or without the seller's permission.
2
Distinguish between value (qimah) and price (thaman)
Understand the definitions: qimah is the market value as determined by merchants, while thaman is the contractually agreed price. The Hanafi school uses qimah for destruction because the buyer's possession is like a deposit before ownership is complete.
For fungible items (mithli), the buyer guarantees a similar item (mithl), not value, due to riba considerations.
3
Apply the same principle to permanent defects
If a permanent defect (like amputation of a limb) occurs in the buyer's hand, the seller may enforce the sale or rescind and claim compensation for the decrease. The buyer owes the price (thaman) for permanent defects, not value. Temporary defects (like illness) leave the buyer on option until resolved.
For fungibles, the seller cannot claim decrease compensation due to suspicion of riba.
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad hold that for destruction, the buyer pays the price (thaman); for permanent defects, he pays the value (qimah). The Hanafi response is that complete ownership occurred before the inability to return, so the sale is binding and the price is owed for permanent defects, but for destruction, the value is owed because possession preceded full ownership.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the amount owed: market value vs. contract price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقبض المشتري المبيع الذي فيه خيار البائع إذا هلك في يده في مدة الخيار. (عيني) يهلك بالقيمة: [ أي البدل؛ ليعم المثلي إذا قبضه بإذن البائع. (ط)] مطلقاً سواء قبض بإذن البائع أو بغير إذنه، حتى يلزم المشتري قيمته يوم القبض إن كان من ذوات القيم، وإلا فيجب ضمان مثله إن كان مثلياً، وعند الشافعي وأحمد: يهلك بالثمن مطلقاً، ولو هلك في يد البائع انفسخ البيع، فلا شيء له على المشتري كما في البيع الصحيح المطلق، ولو تعيب في يد المشتري، فللبائع أن يلزم البيع إن شاء، وإن شاء فسخ البيع وضمنه النقصان إذا كان قيمياً. فلو كان مثلياً ليس له تضمينه النقصان لشبهة الربا، ولو تعيب في يد البائع فهو على خياره، ولكن المشتري إن شاء أخذه بجميع الثمن، وإن شاء فسخ كما في البيع المطلق، وإذا كان العيب بفعل البائع تسقط حصته من الثمن؛ لأن ما يحدث بفعله يكون مضموناً عليه رمز الحقائق (۱۲/۲ ، ۱۳] ثم اعلم أن القيمة يطلق على الذي عند التجار أي المالية التي يعرفونها أهل السوق، والثمن يطلق على الذي تقرر بين العاقدين سواء كان أقل من أصل القيمة أو أكثر. (فتح، محشي)
وبقبضه يهلك بالثمن يعني يلزمه الثمن بسبب قبضه المبيع الذي فيه خياره إذا هلك في يده؛ لأنه لما قرب إلى الهلاك عجز عن رده، فيلزم البيع، فعليه ثمنه، وعند الشافعي في قول: لزمته القيمة؛ لأنه عجز عن الرد قبل تمام الملك. رمز الحقائق: ۱۳/۲] قلنا إن تمام الملك حصل له قبل العجز والحاصل أن الهلاك لا يعري عن 
مقدمة عيب 
يمنع الرد فيهلك، وقد انبرم البيع فيلزم الثمن، ولا يكون أدنى حالا من المقبوض على سوم الشراء. (فتح) كتعيبه: [ أي كما يلزمه الثمن إذا دخل في المبيع عيب لا يرتفع كقطع اليد، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خياره. (عيني)] أي كما لو تعيب المبيع في يد المشتري وكان الخيار له تجب القيمة أو الثمن مطلقا، سواء كان بفعله أو بفعل أجنبي أو بآفة سماوية أو بفعل المبيع، والمراد بالعيب عيب لا يرتفع كقطع العضو، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خيار، فإن ارتفع المرض في المدة لا يلزمه وإلا لزمه وعن الشافعي يلزمه القيمة في التعيب أيضاً. رمز الحقائق: ١٣/٢] (فتح)
And by the buyer's taking possession of the sold item which has the seller's option, if it is destroyed in his hand during the option period. (Ayni) It is destroyed by value: i.e., the substitute; to include fungible items if he took possession with the seller's permission. (T) Absolutely, whether he took possession with the seller's permission or without it, so that the buyer is liable for its value on the day of taking possession if it is of those measured by value, otherwise he must guarantee a similar item if it is fungible. And according to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad: it is destroyed by the price absolutely. And if it is destroyed in the seller's hand, the sale is rescinded, and there is nothing for him against the buyer, as in the absolute valid sale. And if it becomes defective in the buyer's hand, the seller may enforce the sale if he wishes, or if he wishes rescind the sale and guarantee the decrease if it is a value-based item. If it is fungible, he cannot make him guarantee the decrease due to the suspicion of riba. And if it becomes defective in the seller's hand, then he is on his option, but the buyer may take it at the full price if he wishes, or rescind as in the absolute sale. And if the defect is by the seller's action, his share of the price is dropped because what occurs by his action is guaranteed upon him. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 12/2, 13) Then know that 'value' (qimah) refers to what is with the merchants, i.e., the monetary value that the market knows, and 'price' (thaman) refers to what is agreed between the contracting parties, whether less or more than the original value. (Fath, Muhashi) And by his taking possession it is destroyed by the price, i.e., he is liable for the price due to his taking possession of the sold item which has his option if it is destroyed in his hand; because when it is about to be destroyed, he is unable to return it, so the sale is binding, so he owes its price. And according to al-Shafi'i in one opinion: he is liable for the value because he is unable to return before complete ownership. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 13/2) We said: complete ownership occurred for him before the inability. The conclusion is that destruction does not lack a prior defect that prevents return, so the sale is consummated and the price is owed, and it is not inferior to an item taken on the basis of a purchase negotiation. (Fath) Like its defect: i.e., just as he is liable for the price if a defect enters the sold item that does not disappear, like amputation of a hand, while if it is temporary like illness, he is on his option. (Ayni) i.e., just as if the sold item becomes defective in the buyer's hand and he has the option, the value or price is owed absolutely, whether by his act or by an outsider's act or by a natural calamity or by the item's own act. The meaning of defect is a defect that does not disappear, like amputation of a limb; if it does disappear like illness, then he is on his option: if the illness ends within the period, he is not liable; otherwise he is liable. And from al-Shafi'i: he is liable for the value in case of defect also. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 13/2) (Fath)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability for the sold item if it is destroyed or becomes defective while in the buyer's possession during the option period (khiyar al-shart). It begins by stating the Hanafi position: if the item with the seller's option is destroyed in the buyer's hand, the buyer must pay its value (qimah) – meaning the market value on the day of taking possession – regardless of whether he took possession with or without the seller's permission. This applies both to non-fungibles (qimiyyat) and fungibles (mithliyyat). In contrast, al-Shafi'i and Ahmad hold that the buyer is liable for the agreed price (thaman). The passage explains the reasoning: the buyer's inability to return triggers the binding of the sale. Then it discusses defects: if a permanent defect (like loss of a limb) occurs in the buyer's hand, the seller may either enforce the sale or rescind and claim compensation for the decrease in value. For fungibles, compensation for decrease is not allowed due to riba. If the defect is in the seller's hand, the buyer may take the item at full price or rescind. If the seller caused the defect, he bears the loss. The passage clarifies that 'value' is market price, while 'price' is the contractual amount. There is also a brief mention of the Shafi'i view that the buyer pays value if the defect occurs, contrasting with the Hanafi view that he pays the price.

Key Terms
قيمة (qimah): Market value of an item, determined by merchants.
ثمن (thaman): The price agreed upon in the contract.
عيب (ayb): A defect in the sold item that is permanent (like amputation) or temporary (like illness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a non-fungible item sold with khiyar al-shart for the seller (the buyer is the one with possession) is destroyed in the buyer's hand, what must the buyer pay?
A) The agreed price (thaman).
B) The market value (qimah) on the day he took possession.
C) Nothing, because the sale is void.
D) Half the price.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-shart, destruction in buyer's hand triggers compensation at market value, while permanent defect triggers the contract price, with a distinction between fungible and non-fungible goods due to riba concerns.

Buying One's Wife with Khiyar al-Shart
First subsidiary ruling on buying wife with option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purchasing one's own wife with khiyar al-shart and explain the consequence of intercourse during the option period.

Core Idea
Buying your wife with an option does not end the marriage; intercourse binds the sale but you may still return her if undamaged.

When a man buys his own wife who is a slave with an option (khiyar) stipulated for him, the marriage remains intact because ownership is not transferred during the option period. This lesson clarifies the ruling and the effect of intercourse, including a comparison with the Shafi'i position on destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A husband buys his slave wife with khiyar al-shart for the buyer (option to confirm or cancel). The wife is owned by another man.
The wife is a slave; this is specific to historical context.
2
State the ruling on marriage
The marriage remains valid during the option period. The husband does not become her owner until the sale is final.
This is from Abu Hanifa; the option does not affect the marital contract.
3
Consequence of intercourse
If the husband has intercourse, the sale becomes binding and he owes the price (not the value). He loses the right to return her because defloration is a defect.
Intercourse is treated as acceptance of the sale, not as a breach of marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو اشترى زوجته بالخيار بقي النكاح، فإن وطئها يعني يلزمه الثمن لا القيمة بأن كانت أمة لرجل أي بخيار الزوج المشتري له أن يردّها، ولو أجاز من له الخيار بغيبة صاحبه صح، البيع ولو أجنبيا وبقبضه يهلك بالثمن يعني يلزمه الثمن بسبب قبضه المبيع الذي فيه خياره إذا هلك في يده؛ لأنه لما قرب إلى الهلاك عجز عن رده، فيلزم البيع، فعليه ثمنه، وعند الشافعي في قول: لزمته القيمة؛ لأنه عجز عن الرد قبل تمام الملك. رمز الحقائق: ۱۳/۲] قلنا إن تمام الملك حصل له قبل العجز والحاصل أن الهلاك لا يعري عن 
مقدمة عيب 
يمنع الرد فيهلك، وقد انبرم البيع فيلزم الثمن، ولا يكون أدنى حالا من المقبوض على سوم الشراء. (فتح) 
..
ولو أجاز من له الخيار بغيبة صاحبه صح، البيع ولو أجنبيا، له الخيار بائعاً كان أو مشترياً أو أجنبياً. بغيبة صاحبه [ أي البائع إن كان الخيار للمشتري والمشتري إن كان الخيار للبائع ] المراد بالغيبة عدم علمه، وبالحضرة علمه (عيني) صح : [ أي الإجازة؛ لأنه إسقاط حقه فلا يعتبر حضور من عليه الحق كالطلاق والعتاق (عيني)] أي الإجازة مطلقاً، سواء كانت صريحاً بأن يقول: من أجزته أو أخذته، أو دلالة بأن يتصرف البائع في ثمن المبيع أو المشتري في المبيع تصرف الملاك. (عيني)
If he buys his wife with option, the marriage remains. Then if he has intercourse with her, it means he is liable for the price, not the value, if she was a slave woman belonging to a man, i.e., with the option of the husband-buyer he may return her. And if the one who has the option gives acceptance while his partner is absent, the sale is valid. Even if a stranger... And by his taking possession it is destroyed by the price... (then repetition) ... And if the one who has the option gives acceptance while his partner is absent, the sale is valid, even if a stranger. The one with the option may be seller, buyer, or a stranger. 'In the absence of his partner' means the seller if the option is for the buyer, and the buyer if the option is for the seller. The meaning of absence is lack of knowledge, and presence is knowledge. (Ayni) 'Valid': i.e., the acceptance; because it is dropping of his right, so the presence of the one against whom the right is held is not a consideration, like divorce and manumission. (Ayni) That is, the acceptance absolutely, whether explicitly by saying: 'I have given acceptance' or 'I have taken it', or implicitly by the seller dealing with the price or the buyer dealing with the sold item as owners. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents two subsidiary rulings branching from the principles of khiyar al-shart. First, if a man buys his own wife (assuming she is a slave) with an option stipulated for him, the marriage contract remains valid and is not dissolved by the purchase. This is because, according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer does not own the item during the option period, so the wife does not become his property, and the marriage continues. If he has intercourse with her during the option period, he becomes liable for the price (not the value) as the sale becomes binding. He still has the right to return her if she is defective but not if he caused a defect like defloration. The second ruling is about acceptance (ijazah) of the option contract. Whoever has the right to cancel or confirm the sale may do so even if the other party is absent. 'Absence' means the other party is unaware of the acceptance; it is not a condition that he be present. The acceptance can be explicit (e.g., saying 'I accept' or 'I take') or implicit through actions that indicate ownership, such as the seller using the price or the buyer using the item. This is because acceptance is merely dropping one's right, which does not require the presence of the other party, analogous to divorce or manumission.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Ratification or acceptance of a contract during the option period.
الغيبة (al-ghaybah): Absence of one party; here meaning lack of knowledge of the other party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man buys his wife (a slave) with khiyar al-shart and then has intercourse during the option period, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The marriage is dissolved immediately.
B) He must pay the price and may still return her if undamaged.
C) He owes no payment because the option is still active.
D) He must pay the value and the marriage is void.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart does not dissolve a concurrent valid contract like marriage; intercourse during option binds the sale and obliges payment of the price.

Acceptance (Ijazah) in Absence
Second subsidiary ruling on acceptance in absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that acceptance (ijazah) in khiyar al-shart is valid even if the other party is absent, and distinguish between explicit and implicit acceptance.

Core Idea
Ijazah is dropping a right; it requires no presence, only knowledge.

In a sale with an option, the party holding the right to confirm or cancel may do so even if the other party is not physically present. The Hanafi school defines 'absence' as lack of knowledge, not physical location. This lesson explains the validity and forms of acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Define absence
Absence (ghaybah) means the other party is unaware of the acceptance, not necessarily physically far. If the other party knows, it is considered attendance (hadrah).
This definition is from Ayni's commentary.
2
Forms of acceptance
Acceptance can be explicit (saying 'I accept' or 'I take') or implicit (acting as owner, like the seller using the price or the buyer using the item).
Implicit acceptance is valid because it indicates exercise of the right.

Liability for Destruction and Permanent Defect During Khiyar al-Shart
Ruling on buyer's liability for destruction and permanent defect during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a purchased item perishes or acquires a permanent defect during khiyar al-shart, explain the proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
If the item perishes or gets a permanent defect during khiyar, the buyer owes the agreed price—not market value.

When a buyer takes possession of an item under khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), the sale is not yet binding. But if the item is destroyed or suffers a permanent defect, the Hanafi school holds that the buyer must pay the full agreed price, not the market value. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the buyer's possession of an item during khiyar al-shart. The ruling: if the item perishes or gets a permanent defect, the buyer owes the price (thaman).
This is a wajib obligation—the buyer must pay.
2
Understand the reasoning
The destruction or permanent defect prevents the buyer from returning the item, so the sale becomes binding (lazim). The buyer's ownership was complete before the inability to return.
The Hanafi key argument: 'it is not less than that taken possession of under a promise to purchase'.
3
Distinguish permanent vs temporary defect
If the defect is permanent (e.g., amputation), liability is immediate. If temporary (e.g., illness), the option continues; if cured within the period, no liability; if not, sale binds.
The distinction determines when the obligation is triggered.
4
Locate the proof
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the case of al-maqbud 'ala sawm al-shira' (possession under a promise to purchase), where liability for the price is established.
The Hanafi use this analogy to show the buyer's position is not weaker.
5
Compare with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds the buyer owes the market value (qima) because ownership was incomplete when the inability to return occurred.
The practical difference: price vs. value may diverge if market changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقبضه يهلك بالثمن كتعيبه، يعني يلزمه الثمن بسبب قبضه المبيع الذي فيه خياره إذا هلك في يده؛ لأنه لما قرب إلى الهلاك عجز عن رده، فيلزم البيع، فعليه ثمنه، وعند الشافعي في قول: لزمته القيمة؛ لأنه عجز عن الرد قبل تمام الملك. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۳/۲] قلنا إن تمام الملك حصل له قبل العجز والحاصل أن الهلاك لا يعري عن مقدمة عيب يمنع الرد فيهلك، وقد انبرم البيع فيلزم الثمن، ولا يكون أدنى حالا من المقبوض على سوم الشراء. (فتح) كتعيبه: [ أي كما يلزمه الثمن إذا دخل في المبيع عيب لا يرتفع كقطع اليد، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خياره. (عيني)] أي كما لو تعيب المبيع في يد المشتري وكان الخيار له تجب القيمة أو الثمن مطلقا، سواء كان بفعله أو بفعل أجنبي أو بآفة سماوية أو بفعل المبيع، والمراد بالعيب عيب لا يرتفع كقطع العضو، وإن كان يرتفع كالمرض فهو على خيار، فإن ارتفع المرض في المدة لا يلزمه وإلا لزمه وعن الشافعي يلزمه القيمة في التعيب أيضاً. [رمز الحقائق: ١٣/٢] (فتح)
And with his taking possession, if it perishes, [it is] with the price, like its becoming defective: meaning he is obligated for the price because of his taking possession of the sold item that has his option if it perishes in his hand; because when it is near to perishing he becomes unable to return it, so the sale becomes binding, so he owes its price. And according to al-Shafi'i in one opinion: he owes the value; because he became unable to return before complete ownership. [Code of Realities: 13/2] We said that complete ownership occurred for him before the inability, and the conclusion is that destruction is not free from the introduction of a defect that prevents return so it perishes, and the sale has been concluded so the price is owed, and it is not less than that which is taken possession of under a promise to purchase. (Fath) Like its becoming defective: [ i.e., as the price is owed if a defect that does not disappear enters the sold item, like cutting off a hand, and if it disappears like illness, he remains on his option. (Ayni) ] i.e., just as if the sold item becomes defective in the buyer's hand and he has the option, the value or price is owed absolutely, whether by his action, the action of a stranger, an act of God, or the action of the sold item. And what is meant by defect is a defect that does not disappear, like cutting off a limb; and if it disappears like illness, he remains on his option: if the illness disappears within the period, he is not obligated; otherwise he is obligated. And al-Shafi'i says: he owes the value in the case of defect as well. [Code of Realities: 13/2] (Fath)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It addresses the liability of a buyer who has khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). The core ruling is: if the purchased item perishes (halak) while in the buyer's possession, the buyer must pay the agreed price (thaman), not the market value (qima). The reason is that the buyer's possession under khiyar is akin to possession under a valid sale; the destruction prevents return, so the sale becomes binding (lazim). The Hanafi school further argues that complete ownership (tam al-milk) is established before the inability to return, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who says ownership is incomplete until the option period ends, so the value is owed. The same principle applies to permanent defects ('ayb) like amputation: the buyer becomes liable. If the defect is temporary (e.g., illness), the option continues; if it is cured within the period, no liability; if not, the sale becomes binding. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) by analogy to the case of possession under a promise to purchase (al-maqbud 'ala sawm al-shira').

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of stipulation where one or both parties have the right to cancel the sale within a specified period.
الثمن (thaman): The agreed-upon sale price.
القيمة (qima): The market value of the item at the time of destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a buyer with khiyar al-shart takes possession of the item and it perishes, what is he obligated to pay?
A) The market value (qima)
B) The agreed price (thaman)
C) Nothing, because the sale is void
D) Half the price

Key Takeaway
During khiyar al-shart, destruction or permanent defect makes the sale binding and the buyer owes the agreed price.

Purchase of One's Wife Under Khiyar al-Shart: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and its effect on marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of khiyar al-shart on marriage when a man buys his slave-wife, and determine whether return is possible after intercourse.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart prevents ownership according to Abu Hanifa, preserving marriage; according to the Sahibayn, it does not, dissolving the marriage.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq examines a branch case rooted in a fundamental intra-Hanafi disagreement: does the buyer's option (khiyar al-mushtari) block the transfer of ownership during the option period? The answer determines whether a man who buys his own slave-wife can remain married to her and whether he can return her after intercourse. Both positions are presented with their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that the dispute centers on whether khiyar al-mushtari prevents ownership transfer during the option period. Abu Hanifa says yes; the Sahibayn say no.
This is the root of the branch case.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
According to Abu Hanifa, khiyar prevents the sold item from entering the buyer's ownership. Hence, the marriage remains valid because the wife is not owned.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, khiyar does not prevent ownership; ownership transfers immediately. Therefore, the marriage dissolves upon purchase.
4
Apply to the case of intercourse
Under Abu Hanifa, if the buyer has intercourse with the slave-wife, it is by virtue of marriage. He can still return her unless he causes a deficiency (e.g., defloration). Under the Sahibayn, intercourse is by virtue of ownership (milk al-yamin), so return is entirely prevented.
The same applies to kissing or touching with desire.
5
Note the extensions
The passage notes that al-Ayni and al-Zayla'i list many derivative cases all built on this disputed principle.
Comprehensive coverage is found in their works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو اشترى زوجته إلخ هذه إحدى المسائل المتفرعة على الأصل المختلف فيه، وهو أن خيار المشتري مانع عن ملكه للمبيع عند الإمام خلافاً لهما بقي النكاح لأن خيار المشتري يمنع دخول المبيع في ملكه عند الإمام، وعندهما: يفسد النكاح؛ لدخولها في ملكه. فإن وطئها: [ أي الأمة المذكور في مدة الخيار. (عيني)] أي إذا لم ينقصها الوطء، فإن نقصها ولو ثيباً امتنع الرد؛ لأنها تعيبت به كما إذا كانت بكراً فوطئها وأزال بكارتها، أو أفضاها، فإنه لا يردها كما في المتن، وليس له أن يردها عليه بعد ما تعيب عنده، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وعندهما: ليس له أن يردها مطلقاً، سواء تعيبت بالوطء أولا؛ لأن النكاح انفسخ بملكه إياها، فيكون الوطء بحكم ملك اليمين فيمنع الرد كما إذا اشترى غير زوجته فوطئها، وكذا لو وطئها غير الزوج في يده، ولو لم ينقصها الوطء، وكذا إذا قبلها أو مسها أو مسته بشهوة، وقد ذكر العيني في "المستجمع شرح المجمع" عشر مسائل وذكر الزيلعي أربعا أخرى كلها مبنية على الأصل المختلف فيه بينه وبين الصاحبين من شاء الاستيعاب فليرجع إلى العيني. عيني، فتح محشي يردها: لأن الوطء بحكم النكاح لا بحكم ملك اليمين. (عيني)
If he purchases his wife etc.: This is one of the branch issues based on the disputed principle: that the buyer's option prevents his ownership of the sold item according to the Imam, contrary to the two companions. The marriage remains because the buyer's option prevents the sold item from entering his ownership according to the Imam. According to them: the marriage becomes invalid because she enters his ownership. If he has intercourse with her: [ i.e., the aforementioned slave woman during the option period. (Ayni) ] i.e., if the intercourse does not diminish her; if it diminishes her, even if she is a non-virgin, return is prevented because she became defective by it, just as if she was a virgin and he had intercourse and removed her virginity, or made her ifda', then he does not return her as in the text, and he cannot return her to him after she became defective in his possession, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. According to them: he cannot return her at all, whether she became defective by intercourse or not, because the marriage was dissolved by his ownership of her, so the intercourse is by virtue of right hand possession and prevents return, just as if he bought a non-wife and had intercourse with her, and similarly if a non-husband had intercourse with her in his hand even if it did not diminish her, and similarly if he kissed her or touched her or she touched him with desire. And al-Ayni has mentioned in al-Mustajma' Sharh al-Majma' ten issues, and al-Zayla'i mentioned four others, all built on the disputed principle between him and the two companions. Whoever wishes comprehensive coverage should refer to al-Ayni. (Ayni, Fath, with marginal notes) He returns her: because intercourse is by virtue of marriage, not by virtue of right hand possession. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on a derivative case from the fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart. The issue: if a man buys his own wife (a slave belonging to another) with a khiyar, what happens to the marriage? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer's option (khiyar al-mushtari) prevents the transfer of ownership during the option period. Hence, the marriage remains valid. If he has intercourse with her, he must pay the price (thaman), not the value, and the act is considered by virtue of marriage, not ownership. He can still return her unless he causes a diminution (e.g., defloration). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that khiyar does not prevent ownership; thus, the purchase immediately transfers ownership, dissolving the marriage. Therefore, he cannot return her after intercourse regardless of deficiency. The text also notes that if a stranger (non-husband) has intercourse with her in the buyer's possession, the ruling follows the same principle. The commentary references extensive treatment by al-Ayni and al-Zayla'i.

Key Terms
خيار المشتري (khiyar al-mushtari): The buyer's option in a sale with khiyar al-shart.
ملك اليمين (milk al-yamin): Ownership by right hand possession, i.e., ownership that allows intercourse with a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a man buys his slave-wife with khiyar al-shart and has intercourse with her without causing deficiency, can he return her?
A) Yes, because the marriage remains and he can return her
B) No, because the marriage is dissolved
C) Yes, but only after paying the value
D) No, because intercourse always prevents return

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-shart prevents ownership transfer according to Abu Hanifa, so the marriage continues and return is possible unless deficiency occurs; the Sahibayn hold the opposite.

Validity of Ratification in the Absence of the Other Party
Ruling on ratification with khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ratification of a sale in the absence of the other party and explain the legal reasoning based on isqat.

Core Idea
Ratification is valid even if the other party is absent because it is a unilateral relinquishment of right.

This lesson examines a key principle in sales law: the validity of ratification (ijaza) when one party has an option. The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, with commentary by al-Ayni, establishes that ratification is effective even without the other party's presence. Understanding this ruling clarifies the nature of ijaza as a unilateral act of relinquishment (isqat), analogous to divorce and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties with khiyar
The passage states that the option (khiyar) exists for the seller, buyer, or a third party (ajnabi). Recognize that any of these can validly ratify.
2
State the ruling on absence
The core ruling: ratification (ijaza) is valid even if the other party (the counterpart) is absent or unaware. This is the main legal conclusion.
3
Understand the rationale (talil)
The reason given: ratification is a relinquishment (isqat) of the ratifier's own right. Like divorce (talaq) and manumission (itaq), it does not require the presence of the affected party because the one holding the right is unilaterally dropping it.
The analogy to talaq and itaq is critical: both are unilateral acts that take effect without the other's acceptance.
4
Distinguish explicit and implicit ratification
Ratification can be explicit (saying 'I ratify' or 'I take') or implicit through conduct indicating ownership (e.g., seller using the price, buyer using the item as an owner). Both modes are valid.
Implicit ratification (dalalah) is a key Hanafi concept: actions speak as loud as words when they unequivocally show intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له الخيار بائعاً كان أو مشترياً أو أجنبياً. بغيبة صاحبه صح : [ أي الإجازة؛ لأنه إسقاط حقه فلا يعتبر حضور من عليه الحق كالطلاق والعتاق (عيني)] أي الإجازة مطلقاً، سواء كانت صريحاً بأن يقول: أجزته أو أخذته، أو دلالة بأن يتصرف البائع في ثمن المبيع أو المشتري في المبيع تصرف الملاك. (عيني)
The option exists for the seller, the buyer, or a stranger. In the absence of his counterpart, ratification is valid: [ i.e., ratification; because it is a relinquishment of his right, so the presence of the one on whom the right is held is not considered, like divorce and manumission. (Ayni) ] i.e., ratification absolutely, whether explicit by saying 'I ratify it' or 'I take it', or by indication that the seller deals with the price of the sold item or the buyer deals with the sold item as owners do. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: the person who has the khiyar (whether seller, buyer, or a third party who has been granted the option) can ratify the sale (ijaza) even if the other party is absent (unaware). The reason is that ratification is essentially a relinquishment (isqat) of one's own right, similar to divorce (talaq) and manumission ('itaq), which do not require the presence of the person affected. Ratification can be explicit (by saying 'I ratify' or 'I take') or implicit (by conduct indicating ownership, such as the seller using the price or the buyer using the item as an owner).

Key Terms
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification or acceptance of the sale, ending the option.
إسقاط (isqat): Relinquishment or dropping of a right.
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to cancel or confirm a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because it is a relinquishment of right
B) No, because it requires mutual consent
C) Yes, but only if the absent party later agrees
D) No, because absence invalidates any transaction

Key Takeaway
Ratification (ijaza) is a unilateral relinquishment (isqat) of the option right and is valid even if the counterpart is absent.

Invalidity of Unilateral Rescission Without Knowledge
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on fasakh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasakh without knowledge, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and explain the rationale for the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Fasakh without the other party's knowledge is invalid because it causes potential harm, unlike ratification.

This passage addresses a key scenario in khiyar contracts: can the party with the option unilaterally rescind without informing the other? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, with the majority (Sahibayn) ruling it invalid. We will examine the proofs and understand why the mufta bihi position considers the other party's knowledge essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the exact ruling being discussed? A person with khiyar al-shart rescinds the sale without the counterpart's knowledge. The initial statement says it is not valid (la yasihh).
The base text from Kanz al-Daqaiq states this.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it invalid; Abu Yusuf alone holds it valid, analogizing to ratification (ijaza).
The text says 'عند الطرفين' (at the two companions) and mentions Abu Yusuf's view.
3
Analyze the proof of the Sahibayn
Their proof is based on potential harm: the other party may have relied on the sale, causing loss if the option is for the seller (e.g., buyer used the item) or if for the buyer (e.g., seller gave up other offers). Thus knowledge is needed to avoid this harm.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof (qiyas with ijaza)
Abu Yusuf argues by analogy: just as ratification (ijaza) by the one with khiyar is valid without knowledge, rescission should also be valid because both are exercises of the authority given by the contract.
The text notes this analogy and rebuts it: rescission is an act of compulsion (ilzam), unlike ratification which is not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: fasakh without knowledge is invalid. The majority view is strengthened by the potential harm and the lack of harm in ijaza.
The passage also notes that khiyar al-ru'yah follows this dispute, and for defects, consensus requires knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فسخ لا، وتم العقد بموته وبمضي المدة والإعتاق وتوابعه، والأخذ بشفعة، .... يصح أي لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين قالت ولو فسخ لا: لو فسخ البيع من له خيار العقد بدون علم صاحبه لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف: أيضاً؛ لأن الغائب مسلط على فسخ البيع حيث خير من له الخيار، فلا يتوقف على علمه كالإجازة، وبه الثلاثة، ولهما: أنه تصرف في حق الغير برفع العقد، ولا يعرى عن مضرة؛ لأنه قد يعتمد تمام البيع السابق، فيتصرف فيه، فتلزمه القيمة بالهلاك فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع، أو لا يطلب لسلعته مشترياً فيما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وهذا نوع ضرر، فيتوقف على العلم، بخلاف الإجازة، فإنه لا إلزام فيها، وكيف يقال: إنه مسلط وصاحبه لا يملك الفسخ، ولا تسليط في غير ما يملكه المسلط، وخيار الرؤية على هذا الخلاف، وفي العيب لا يصح فسخه بدون علمه إجماعا؛ لأنه لا يثبت إلا بالقضاء. (عيني، فتح) موت وتم العقد بموته أي بموت من له الخيار والجنون كالموت وكذا الإغماء، وقيدنا بموت من له الخيار؛ لأن غيره لا يتم به العقد بل الخيار باق لمن شرط له، ولا ينتقل إلى الورثة، وقال الشافعي يورث عنه؛ لأنه حق لازم له في البيع، فيجري فيه الإرث كخيار العيب، وبه قال مالك. ولنا: أن الخيار ليس إلا مشية وإرادة فلا ينتقل عنه؛ لأن الغرض منه التأمل لغرض نفسه، وقد بطلت أهلية التأمل له، بخلاف خيار العيب؛ لأن المورث استحق المبيع سليماً، فكذا الوارث؛ لأنه ورث خياره، وخيار التعيين مثبت للوارث ابتداء؛ لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير، لا أن الخيار يورث [ رمز الحقائق: ١٤/٢] (فتح) المدة: أي مدة الخيار؛ لأن عدم النفاذ كان لتمكنه من الفسخ في المدة فإذا مضت ارتفع المانع فتم العقد. (عيني) والإعتاق [ أي وقد يتم أيضاً إعتاق المشتري بأن عتق العبد ؛ لأن الإعتاق دليل الاستبقاء. (عيني)] عطف على قوله : "بموته" أي يتم العقد أيضاً مع الإعتاق؛ لأنه يعتمد الملك لقوله عليه: "لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم" فهو دليل الاستبقاء، وكذا مع توابع الإعتاق كالتدبير والكتابة إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وكذلك كل تصرف لا يحل إلا في الملك كالوطء والتقبيل واللمس بشهوة يتم به البيع. وكذا كل تصرف لا ينفذ إلا في الملك كالبيع والإجارة، وهذا كله إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، ووجد منه شيء من هذه الأشياء، وإن كان الخيار للبائع، وفعل شيئاً من هذه الأشياء، انفسخ البيع؛ لأنه فسخ حكمي، ولو كان الفعل يحل في غير الملك لا يتم به البيع كالاستخدام والركوب ونحو ذلك؛ لأنه يفعل للامتحان والتجربة، فلا يكون دليل الاستبقاء. [ رمز الحقائق ١٥/٢] (فتح) توابعه أي وكذا يتم العقد مع توابع الإعتاق كالتدبير والكتابة. (عيني) والأخذ بشفعة: ليس الأخذ بقيد؛ لأنه يتم بمجرد الطلب سواء أخذ أم لا، ففي الكلام مضاف محذوف، والأصل: "وطلب الأخذ سواء كان طلب مواثبة أو تقرير وصورته أن يشتري دارا بشرط الخيار، ثم يباع دار أخرى بجنبها، فيأخذها المشتري المشترى بالشفعة تم البيع؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة لا يكون إلا بالملك، فكان دليل الإجازة [رمز الحقائق: ١٥/٢] (فتح)
If he rescinds, it is not valid, and the contract is completed by his death, by the expiry of the period, by manumission and its consequences, and by taking pre-emption. ... it is valid? Actually, the rescission is not valid according to the two companions. They said: if the one who has the option of the contract rescinds the sale without the knowledge of his counterpart, the rescission is not valid according to the two companions. And according to Abu Yusuf: also? because the absent person is authorized to rescind the sale since the one with the option has been given authority, so it does not depend on his knowledge, like ratification. And with him [Abu Yusuf] are the three [others?]. And according to them [the two companions]: it is an action regarding the right of another by lifting the contract, and it is not free from harm because he may have relied on the completion of the previous sale and dealt with it, so the value would be owed if it perishes in the case where the option is for the seller, or he may not seek a buyer for his goods in the case where the option is for the buyer, and this is a type of harm, so it depends on knowledge, unlike ratification, for there is no compulsion in it. And how can it be said that he is authorized while his counterpart does not have the right of rescission? And there is no authorization for something that the authorized person does not own. And the option of sighting is upon this dispute, and in defect, rescission is not valid without his knowledge by consensus because it is only established by judgment. (Ayni, Fath) Death: the contract is completed by his death, i.e., the death of the one with the option, and insanity is like death, and similarly unconsciousness. And we restricted it to the death of the one with the option because in the case of another, the contract is not completed by it; rather the option remains for whom it was stipulated, and it does not transfer to the heirs. And al-Shafi'i said: it is inherited from him because it is a right attached to the sale, so inheritance occurs in it like khiyar al-'ayb, and Malik also said it. For us: the option is nothing but wish and will, so it does not transfer from him because the purpose of it is deliberation for his own self, and the capacity for deliberation has ended for him, contrary to khiyar al-'ayb because the testator deserved the sold item sound, so the heir also because he inherits his option. And khiyar al-ta'yin (option of determination) is established for the heir initially due to mixing of his ownership with ownership of another, not that the option is inherited. [Code of Realities: 14/2] (Fath) The period: i.e., the option period; because non-permanence was due to his ability to rescind during the period, so when it passes, the impediment is removed and the contract is completed. (Ayni) And manumission: [ and also the contract may be completed by the buyer manumitting the slave because manumission is evidence of retention. (Ayni) ] It is conjunct to his statement 'by his death' meaning the contract is also completed with manumission because it relies on ownership due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no manumission in that which the son of Adam does not own.' So it is evidence of retention. Similarly with the consequences of manumission like tadbir and kitaba if the option is for the buyer. And likewise every action that is not permissible except in ownership, like intercourse, kissing, and touching with desire, completes the sale. And likewise every action that is not executable except in ownership, like sale and hire. All this if the option is for the buyer and any of these things occur from him. If the option is for the seller and he does any of these things, the sale is rescinded because it is a constructive rescission. If the action is permissible in non-ownership, the sale is not completed by it, like use and riding and the like, because it is done for testing and experience, so it is not evidence of retention. [Code of Realities: 15/2] (Fath) And its consequences: i.e., the contract is also completed with the consequences of manumission like tadbir and kitaba. (Ayni) And taking pre-emption: taking is not a condition; because it is completed by mere demand whether one takes or not. So in the statement there is an omitted construct, and the original is: 'and the demand of taking, whether it is a demand of immediate taking or a demand of confirmation. And its form: he buys a house with the condition of option, then another adjacent house is sold, and the buyer of the purchased house takes it by pre-emption; the sale is completed because taking by pre-emption is only from ownership, so it is evidence of ratification. [Code of Realities: 15/2] (Fath)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage covers two connected rulings. First: if the party with khiyar attempts to rescind (fasakh) the contract without the knowledge of the other party, it is invalid according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf alone holds it valid, analogizing to ratification. The relied-upon view is the invalidity because rescission affects the other party's rights and may cause harm (e.g., the buyer may have already relied on the sale). Second: the contract becomes final and binding under several conditions: (a) Death of the person with khiyar: the option does not transfer to heirs (unlike Shafi'i and Malik); the contract is completed. (b) Expiry of the option period: the temporary impediment is removed. (c) Manumission of a slave by the buyer: because freeing implies ownership and retention; similarly, tadbir and kitaba. (d) Any action that is only permissible based on ownership, such as intercourse, kissing, selling, or renting. If the seller does such an action, it constitutes constructive rescission. If the buyer does such an action, the contract is confirmed. (e) Taking pre-emption (shuf'a) by the buyer: because shuf'a can only be claimed by an owner, so it proves acceptance.

Key Terms
فسخ (fasakh): Rescission or cancellation of the contract before it becomes binding.
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification or approval of a contract, especially by the person with khiyar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is fasakh without knowledge invalid?
A) Because the other party has the right to rescind as well.
B) Because it may cause harm to the other party who relied on the sale.
C) Because the rescission must be in writing.
D) Because the option period cannot be shortened.

Key Takeaway
Fasakh without the other party's knowledge is invalid in the Hanafi school because it potentially harms the relying party; ratification (ijaza) is distinguished by its lack of compulsion.

Automatic Completion of Khiyar Contract
Ruling on completion events and inheritance dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the events that complete a khiyar contract, explain why manumission confirms ownership, and evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute on inheritance of khiyar.

Core Idea
Death, expiry, manumission, and acts of ownership complete the khiyar contract; the option is not inherited.

The contract with khiyar al-shart remains suspended until one of several events occurs that indicate final approval. This passage details those events and also addresses an important cross-madhhab question: does the option transfer to heirs upon death? The Hanafi school holds it does not, while Shafi'i and Malik differ.

Guided Path
1
List the completion events
Identify all events mentioned that cause the contract to become binding: death of the option holder, expiry of the option period, manumission of a slave by the buyer, actions that imply ownership (intercourse, sale, etc.), and claiming pre-emption.
The order in the text: بموته، وبمضي المدة، والإعتاق وتوابعه، والأخذ بشفعة.
2
Analyze the reasoning for death and expiry
Death ends the capacity for deliberation; the contract becomes binding because the option was personal. Expiry removes the temporary impediment (the option).
3
Explain why manumission and ownership acts complete the contract
Manumission requires ownership; thus freeing a slave proves the buyer considers himself owner, confirming the sale. Similarly, any act only permissible in ownership (like intercourse) shows the intent to retain.
The text cites the hadith: 'La 'itq fi ma la yamlik' as evidence.
4
Distinguish actions that do not complete
Actions permissible in non-ownership (like riding for testing) do not imply ownership; they are for trial and thus do not complete the contract.
5
Examine the inheritance dispute
Hanafi: khiyar al-shart is not inherited because it is a personal wish and intention; Shafi'i and Malik: it is inherited as a right attached to the sale, like khiyar al-'ayb.
The Hanafi proof: the testator's capacity for deliberation ends with death, so the option dies with him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فسخ لا، وتم العقد بموته وبمضي المدة والإعتاق وتوابعه، والأخذ بشفعة، .... يصح أي لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين قالت ولو فسخ لا: لو فسخ البيع من له خيار العقد بدون علم صاحبه لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف: أيضاً؛ لأن الغائب مسلط على فسخ البيع حيث خير من له الخيار، فلا يتوقف على علمه كالإجازة، وبه الثلاثة، ولهما: أنه تصرف في حق الغير برفع العقد، ولا يعرى عن مضرة؛ لأنه قد يعتمد تمام البيع السابق، فيتصرف فيه، فتلزمه القيمة بالهلاك فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع، أو لا يطلب لسلعته مشترياً فيما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وهذا نوع ضرر، فيتوقف على العلم، بخلاف الإجازة، فإنه لا إلزام فيها، وكيف يقال: إنه مسلط وصاحبه لا يملك الفسخ، ولا تسليط في غير ما يملكه المسلط، وخيار الرؤية على هذا الخلاف، وفي العيب لا يصح فسخه بدون علمه إجماعا؛ لأنه لا يثبت إلا بالقضاء. (عيني، فتح) موت وتم العقد بموته أي بموت من له الخيار والجنون كالموت وكذا الإغماء، وقيدنا بموت من له الخيار؛ لأن غيره لا يتم به العقد بل الخيار باق لمن شرط له، ولا ينتقل إلى الورثة، وقال الشافعي يورث عنه؛ لأنه حق لازم له في البيع، فيجري فيه الإرث كخيار العيب، وبه قال مالك. ولنا: أن الخيار ليس إلا مشية وإرادة فلا ينتقل عنه؛ لأن الغرض منه التأمل لغرض نفسه، وقد بطلت أهلية التأمل له، بخلاف خيار العيب؛ لأن المورث استحق المبيع سليماً، فكذا الوارث؛ لأنه ورث خياره، وخيار التعيين مثبت للوارث ابتداء؛ لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير، لا أن الخيار يورث [ رمز الحقائق: ١٤/٢] (فتح) المدة: أي مدة الخيار؛ لأن عدم النفاذ كان لتمكنه من الفسخ في المدة فإذا مضت ارتفع المانع فتم العقد. (عيني) والإعتاق [ أي وقد يتم أيضاً إعتاق المشتري بأن عتق العبد ؛ لأن الإعتاق دليل الاستبقاء. (عيني)] عطف على قوله : "بموته" أي يتم العقد أيضاً مع الإعتاق؛ لأنه يعتمد الملك لقوله عليه: "لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم" فهو دليل الاستبقاء، وكذا مع توابع الإعتاق كالتدبير والكتابة إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وكذلك كل تصرف لا يحل إلا في الملك كالوطء والتقبيل واللمس بشهوة يتم به البيع. وكذا كل تصرف لا ينفذ إلا في الملك كالبيع والإجارة، وهذا كله إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، ووجد منه شيء من هذه الأشياء، وإن كان الخيار للبائع، وفعل شيئاً من هذه الأشياء، انفسخ البيع؛ لأنه فسخ حكمي، ولو كان الفعل يحل في غير الملك لا يتم به البيع كالاستخدام والركوب ونحو ذلك؛ لأنه يفعل للامتحان والتجربة، فلا يكون دليل الاستبقاء. Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption in property sales.
إعتاق (i'taq): Manumission of a slave; in this context, an act that confirms the buyer's ownership and completes the khiyar contract.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect – the buyer's right to return a defective item.

Key Takeaway

Rescission Without Knowledge of Other Party
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of unilateral rescission without knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on unilateral rescission without knowledge and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Rescission of a sale without the other party's knowledge is invalid according to the majority of the Hanafi school due to potential harm.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if a party who holds an option (khiyar al-shart) rescinds the contract without informing the other party, is the rescission valid? The text presents the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani ruling it invalid, while Abu Yusuf considers it valid. This lesson walks through the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rescission of a sale by the option-holder (khiyar al-shart) without the other party's knowledge. The matn says 'ولو فسخ لا' indicating invalidity as the default ruling.
The phrase 'لا يصح الفسخ' (rescission is not valid) is the relied-upon position.
2
Identify the two positions within the school
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that rescission without knowledge is invalid. Abu Yusuf holds that it is valid, likening it to ijaza (acceptance of authorization).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; all three are within the same school.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the option-holder is authorized (musallat) to rescind, just as a person authorized to accept an offer (ijaza) can do so without the other party's knowledge. Thus, knowledge is not a condition.
His key analogy: 'كالإجازة' (like the acceptance of authorization).
4
Understand the majority's proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that rescission is a disposition affecting the other party's rights and causes harm (darar). The other party may have relied on the contract (e.g., sold the item, or refrained from selling elsewhere). Hence, it depends on knowledge to prevent harm.
They distinguish ijaza because ijaza does not compel obligations, whereas rescission removes existing obligations.
5
Note the scope and consensus
The same dispute applies to khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection). However, for khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), there is consensus that rescission without knowledge is invalid because it requires a court judgment (qada').
This shows that the ikhtilaf is specific to khiyar al-shart and al-ru'ya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فسخ لا أي لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين قالت ولو فسخ لا: لو فسخ البيع من له خيار العقد بدون علم صاحبه لا يصح الفسخ عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف: أيضاً؛ لأن الغائب مسلط على فسخ البيع حيث خير من له الخيار، فلا يتوقف على علمه كالإجازة، وبه الثلاثة، ولهما: أنه تصرف في حق الغير برفع العقد، ولا يعرى عن مضرة؛ لأنه قد يعتمد تمام البيع السابق، فيتصرف فيه، فتلزمه القيمة بالهلاك فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع، أو لا يطلب لسلعته مشترياً فيما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وهذا نوع ضرر، فيتوقف على العلم، بخلاف الإجازة، فإنه لا إلزام فيها، وكيف يقال: إنه مسلط وصاحبه لا يملك الفسخ، ولا تسليط في غير ما يملكه المسلط، وخيار الرؤية على هذا الخلاف، وفي العيب لا يصح فسخه بدون علمه إجماعا؛ لأنه لا يثبت إلا بالقضاء. (عيني، فتح)
And if he rescinds, not [valid]. He said: The rescission is not valid according to the two parties. She said: And if he rescinds, no: If the one who has the option of the contract rescinds the sale without the knowledge of his companion, the rescission is not valid according to the two parties. And according to Abu Yusuf, also; because the absent one is authorized to rescind the sale since the one having the option was given choice, so it does not depend on his knowledge like the [acceptance of] authorization, and with him the three. And for the two: it is a disposition regarding the right of another by cancellation of the contract, and it is not free from harm; because he may have relied on the completion of the previous sale and disposed of it, so the price becomes binding upon destruction if the option is for the seller, or he may not find a buyer for his goods if the option is for the buyer, and this is a type of harm, so it depends on knowledge, unlike authorization, for there is no compulsion in it. And how is it said that he is authorized while his companion does not have the right to rescind, and there is no authorization in something that the authorized does not possess. The option of inspection is upon this difference of opinion, and regarding the defect, rescission without knowledge is invalid by consensus, because it is only established by judgment. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of rescinding a sale by the party having khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) without the other party's knowledge. The matn states 'ولو فسخ لا' indicating invalidity. The commentary explains that this is the view of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani). According to Abu Yusuf, he also deems it invalid? The text says 'also' but his reasoning suggests validity—this is a textual ambiguity. In standard Hanafi fiqh, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that rescission without knowledge is invalid due to potential harm to the other party who may have acted in reliance. Abu Yusuf holds it valid because the party with the option is authorized to rescind independently, similar to accepting an authorization (ijaza) which does not require knowledge. The reasoning of the two (Sahibayn) for invalidity is that it is a disposition affecting the other's right and causes harm, thus it depends on knowledge. The same ikhtilaf applies to khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection). However, for khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), there is consensus that rescission without knowledge is invalid because it requires a court judgment.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to rescind within a specified period.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of inspection, allowing the buyer to rescind after seeing the purchased item if it is not as expected.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect, allowing the buyer to return a defective item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the ruling on rescinding a sale with khiyar al-shart without the other party's knowledge?
A) Valid, because the option-holder is authorized
B) Invalid, due to potential harm to the other party
C) Valid only if the other party later consents
D) Invalid only if the option is for the buyer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rescission of a sale without the other party's knowledge is invalid according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), with Abu Yusuf dissenting; the same applies to khiyar al-ru'ya, but khiyar al-'ayb requires a court judgment.

8 min
Death of the Option-Holder: Does the Option Transfer to Heirs?
Ruling that contract is completed by death of the party with option, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the death of an option-holder (khiyar al-shart) and distinguish it from khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin.

Core Idea
The option of stipulation dies with its holder; only rights to a sound item are inherited.

When a party with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) dies, does the contract become binding, or can heirs step into the option? The Hanafi school holds that the contract is completed and the option is not inherited, because the option is purely about personal deliberation. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree, considering it a transferable property right. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof, the dispute, and the crucial distinctions between different types of options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: the contract is completed (binding) upon the death of the option-holder. Note that insanity and unconsciousness have the same effect.
The ruling applies to death of the party who has the option, not the other party.
2
Understand the Rationale
The Hanafi rationale: khiyar al-shart is based on wish and will (mashiyyah wa iradah). Its purpose is personal deliberation, which ceases with death. Therefore, the right does not transfer.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, not a transmitted text.
3
Examine the Dispute
Al-Shafi'i and Malik argue that the option is a fixed right in the sale, inheritable like khiyar al-'ayb. Identify their proof and the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The practical difference: under the opposing view, heirs can rescind; under Hanafi, they cannot.
4
Distinguish Khiyar al-Shart from Khiyar al-'Ayb
Khiyar al-'ayb is a right to a sound item; the deceased was entitled to a sound item, so the heir inherits that right. Khiyar al-shart is only for deliberation, not a vested right.
This distinction is key to the Hanafi response.
5
Distinguish Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) is established for the heir ab initio because of intermixed property, not by inheritance. It is a separate category.
The heir gets the right to choose, but not because the option was inherited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتم العقد بموته أي بموت من له الخيار والجنون كالموت وكذا الإغماء، وقيدنا بموت من له الخيار؛ لأن غيره لا يتم به العقد بل الخيار باق لمن شرط له، ولا ينتقل إلى الورثة، وقال الشافعي يورث عنه؛ لأنه حق لازم له في البيع، فيجري فيه الإرث كخيار العيب، وبه قال مالك. ولنا: أن الخيار ليس إلا مشية وإرادة فلا ينتقل عنه؛ لأن الغرض منه التأمل لغرض نفسه، وقد بطلت أهلية التأمل له، بخلاف خيار العيب؛ لأن المورث استحق المبيع سليماً، فكذا الوارث؛ لأنه ورث خياره، وخيار التعيين مثبت للوارث ابتداء؛ لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير، لا أن الخيار يورث [ رمز الحقائق: ١٤/٢] (فتح)
And the contract is completed by his death, i.e., the death of the one who has the option, and insanity is like death, and similarly unconsciousness. We restricted it to the death of the one who has the option because otherwise the contract is not completed by it; rather the option remains for the one for whom it was stipulated, and it does not transfer to the heirs. Al-Shafi'i said it is inherited from him because it is a right attached to him in the sale, so inheritance applies to it like the option of defect, and Malik said the same. And for us: The option is nothing but wish and will, so it does not transfer from him; because its purpose is deliberation for his own interest, and his capacity for deliberation has become void, unlike the option of defect, because the deceased was entitled to the sold item soundly, so likewise the heir, because he inherited his option. And the option of specification is established for the heir ab initio, due to the mixing of his property with that of others, not that the option is inherited. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 14/2] (Fath)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage rules that the contract with khiyar al-shart becomes binding (completed) upon the death of the party who held the option. This applies equally to insanity and unconsciousness, as they remove the capacity for deliberation. The option does not transfer to the heirs, because it is a personal right based on will and deliberation, which ceases with death. Al-Shafi'i and Malik disagree, holding that the option is inheritable like khiyar al-'ayb, because it is a fixed right in the sale. The Hanafi response distinguishes: khiyar al-shart is for personal deliberation, whereas khiyar al-'ayb is a right to a sound item, which the heir inherits. Khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) is different: it is established for the heir initially due to intermixed property, not by inheritance of the option.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation; a contractual right to rescind within a specified period.
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option of specification, where the buyer chooses among multiple items, e.g., in a mixed purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) transfer to the heir upon the death of the option-holder in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, it is inherited like a property right
B) No, the contract becomes binding and the option ceases
C) Yes, but only if the option period has not expired
D) No, unless the heir is also the buyer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-shart is not inherited; the contract is completed upon death of the option-holder.

Contract Completion on Expiry of the Option Period
Expansion of the ruling by al-Ayni

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a contract becomes binding upon expiry of the option period and explain the rationale based on removal of the impediment.

Core Idea
Expiry of the option period automatically completes the contract.

This lesson addresses a key moment in sales with an option: what happens when the stipulated period ends without any action? The Hanafi position, as expanded by Imam al-Ayni, is clear: the contract becomes fully binding. The rationale is that the non-binding status existed only because the option-holder had the right to rescind; once that right expires, the contract is completed. Understanding this rule helps you determine the exact moment when a sale becomes irrevocable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is a sales contract with an option period (khiyar). The ruling is that the contract becomes completed (tamma al-'aqd) when the period expires without any action.
The passage explicitly states: 'fa-idha madat irtafa'a al-mani' fa tamma al-'aqd'.
2
Trace the rationale
Understand why the contract was not fully binding before expiry: the option-holder had the ability to rescind (tamakkun min al-faskh). This ability acted as an impediment (mani') to execution.
3
Identify the condition for the ruling
Note that the ruling presupposes a validly stipulated option period (muddat al-khiyar) that is known and agreed upon by both parties. Without such a valid period, the contract would be immediately binding or have a different rule.
The key term 'muddat al-khiyar' implies a fixed, known duration.
4
Apply the ruling
In a practical scenario: if a buyer has a three-day option to inspect goods and does nothing, after the third day the sale is final and binding. The seller cannot change their mind, and the buyer cannot return the goods without cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المدة: أي مدة الخيار؛ لأن عدم النفاذ كان لتمكنه من الفسخ في المدة فإذا مضت ارتفع المانع فتم العقد. (عيني)
The period: i.e., the period of the option; because the non-execution was due to his ability to rescind during the period, so when it passes, the impediment is removed and the contract is completed. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This short passage explains that the contract is completed when the stipulated option period expires. The reason is that the contract was not fully binding because the option-holder had the right to rescind during that period. Once the period ends, that right is extinguished, and the contract becomes binding and complete. This is a straightforward ruling with no dispute.

Key Terms
مدة الخيار (muddat al-khiyar): The stipulated time period during which the option-holder may rescind the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the seller also gains a right to rescind after the period.
B) Because the option-holder's right to rescind ends, removing the impediment.
C) Because the buyer must accept the goods by then.
D) Because the contract was never valid before expiry.

Key Takeaway
Expiry of a valid option period automatically removes the right to rescind and completes the contract.

Contract Completed by Manumission and Derivatives
Ruling with proof on manumission completing sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that manumission and similar acts complete the sale when performed by the buyer, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish between acts that indicate retention and those that do not.

Core Idea
Manumission by the buyer completes the sale; by the seller, rescinds it. Only acts requiring ownership indicate retention.

In sales with an option period (khiyar al-shart), the parties may perform actions on the subject matter that reveal their intention regarding the contract. This passage explains that certain acts, particularly manumission of a purchased slave, complete the sale because they are only permissible in ownership. The hadith 'There is no manumission in what one does not own' grounds this principle. The passage then extends the ruling to other acts and clarifies the effect when the seller performs such acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
State that manumission by the buyer during the option period completes the sale.
The sale becomes binding (sahih) immediately.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم' (There is no manumission in what the son of Adam does not own).
This is a proof from the Sunnah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Manumission is only valid if one owns the slave. By manumitting, the buyer demonstrates that he considers the slave his property, thereby ratifying the sale.
The hadith implies that manumission requires ownership; performing it proves ownership.
4
Extend to derivatives and similar acts
Tadbir (promise to free after death), kitabah (emancipation contract), and acts only permissible in ownership (intercourse, kissing with desire) or only effective in ownership (selling, leasing) have the same effect.
All these acts indicate the buyer's intention to retain the item.
5
Distinguish by party and act type
If the seller performs such acts, the sale is rescinded. Acts permissible without ownership (e.g., riding, using) do not complete the sale because they are for testing.
The contrast is between acts that require ownership and those that do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإعتاق [ أي وقد يتم أيضاً إعتاق المشتري بأن عتق العبد ؛ لأن الإعتاق دليل الاستبقاء. (عيني)] عطف على قوله : "بموته" أي يتم العقد أيضاً مع الإعتاق؛ لأنه يعتمد الملك لقوله عليه: "لا عتق فيما لا يملك ابن آدم" فهو دليل الاستبقاء، وكذا مع توابع الإعتاق كالتدبير والكتابة إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وكذلك كل تصرف لا يحل إلا في الملك كالوطء والتقبيل واللمس بشهوة يتم به البيع. وكذا كل تصرف لا ينفذ إلا في الملك كالبيع والإجارة، وهذا كله إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، ووجد منه شيء من هذه الأشياء، وإن كان الخيار للبائع، وفعل شيئاً من هذه الأشياء، انفسخ البيع؛ لأنه فسخ حكمي، ولو كان الفعل يحل في غير الملك لا يتم به البيع كالاستخدام والركوب ونحو ذلك؛ لأنه يفعل للامتحان والتجربة، فلا يكون دليل الاستبقاء. [ رمز الحقائق ١٥/٢] (فتح) توابعه أي وكذا يتم العقد مع توابع الإعتاق كالتدبير والكتابة. (عيني)
And manumission [i.e., and the contract may also be completed by the buyer's manumission, i.e., setting free the slave; because manumission is evidence of retention. (Ayni)] It is conjoined to his saying 'by his death': i.e., the contract is also completed with manumission, because it relies on ownership due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no manumission in what the son of Adam does not own.' So it is evidence of retention. Similarly with the derivatives of manumission, such as tadbir and kitabah, if the option is for the buyer. And likewise every disposition that is not permissible except in ownership, such as intercourse, kissing, and touching with desire, completes the sale. And likewise every disposition that is not effective except in ownership, such as sale and lease. All this is if the option is for the buyer and something of these things occurs from him. But if the option is for the seller and he does something of these things, the sale is rescinded, because it is a constructive rescission. And if the act is permissible without ownership, such as using and riding and the like, the sale is not completed by it, because it is done for testing and experimentation, so it is not evidence of retention. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 15/2] (Fath) Its derivatives: i.e., similarly the contract is completed with derivatives of manumission, such as tadbir and kitabah. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage explains that the contract with khiyar al-shart is completed if the buyer performs an act that indicates retention and ownership, such as manumitting the purchased slave. This is based on the hadith 'There is no manumission in what one does not own,' so manumission proves that the buyer considers the slave his property, thus ratifying the sale. Similarly, acts that are only permissible in ownership (like intercourse, kissing with desire) or only effective in ownership (like selling or leasing the item) also complete the sale. However, if the option is for the seller and he performs such acts, it is considered a constructive rescission, not a ratification. Acts that are permissible without ownership, like using or riding, do not complete the sale because they may be done for testing. The derivatives of manumission (tadbir: promise to free after death; kitabah: contract of emancipation) have the same effect as manumission.

Key Terms
الإعتاق (al-iʿtāq): Manumission; freeing a slave.
التدبير (al-tadbīr): A promise to free the slave after the owner's death.
الكتابة (al-kitābah): A contract of emancipation where the slave pays for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is rescinded
B) The sale is completed
C) The option period is extended
D) No effect; option continues

Key Takeaway
Manumission and other ownership-exclusive acts by the buyer complete the sale; by the seller, they rescind it; acts of testing do not affect the contract.

Pre-emption Claim Completes Sale Under Option
Ruling that a pre-emption claim completes the sale during option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a mere demand for pre-emption (shuf'a) during the option period completes the sale, and identify the legal reasoning (dalil aqli) behind it.

Core Idea
Mere demand for pre-emption completes a conditional sale because it implies ownership.

In Hanafi fiqh, a buyer who purchases a property with an option (khayar al-shart) may later claim pre-emption on an adjacent property. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq teaches that such a claim itself, even without taking possession, completes the original sale. Understanding this ruling illuminates how the right of pre-emption interacts with ownership and acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal effect
The buyer's claim to pre-emption (shuf'a) on a neighboring property while under option for another sale is the act in question.
2
Recognize the legal implication
The claim implies the buyer considers himself owner of the first property, because shuf'a is only valid for an owner.
3
Understand the conclusion
Therefore, the option is extinguished and the sale becomes final.
4
Note the absence of requirement for actual taking
The mere talab (demand) suffices; physical taking is not a condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأخذ بشفعة: ليس الأخذ بقيد؛ لأنه يتم بمجرد الطلب سواء أخذ أم لا، ففي الكلام مضاف محذوف، والأصل: "وطلب الأخذ سواء كان طلب مواثبة أو تقرير وصورته أن يشتري دارا بشرط الخيار، ثم يباع دار أخرى بجنبها، فيأخذها المشتري المشترى بالشفعة تم البيع؛ لأن الأخذ بالشفعة لا يكون إلا بالملك، فكان دليل الإجازة رمز الحقائق: ١٥/٢] (فتح)
And the taking by pre-emption: taking is not a condition; because it is completed by mere demand whether he takes or not. So in the speech there is an omitted annexed [word], and the original is: 'And the demand of taking, whether it be demand of prompt or demand of confirmation.' Its form: that he buys a house with an option condition, then another adjacent house is sold, and this buyer takes it by pre-emption, the sale is completed; because taking by pre-emption is only valid with ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 15/2] (Fath)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage explains that taking by pre-emption (shuf'a) completes a sale that was under option. The key point is that it is not the actual taking of possession that matters, but the demand (talab) for pre-emption, because even a mere demand indicates that the buyer considers himself the owner, since pre-emption is only valid if one owns the property. The example: someone buys a house with an option, then another neighboring house is sold. If the buyer claims pre-emption on that neighbor's house, it proves he believes he owns the first house, thus ratifying the sale. Therefore, the option is extinguished and the sale is completed.

Key Terms
شفعة (shufʿa): Pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property from the buyer.
طلب (talab): Demand; the act of claiming pre-emption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Registration of the claim

Key Takeaway
A pre-emption claim during an option period completes the sale because it implies ownership, and mere demand suffices.
