Stipulating Option for a Third Party: Valid by Istihsan
Ruling with proof: validity of third-party option by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates stipulating option for a third party using istihsan, and distinguish between the strict qiyas (Zufar) and the preferred ruling.

Core Idea
Stipulating option for a third party is valid by istihsan because the option is deputized.

In sale contracts, khiyar (option) is typically reserved for the contracting parties. However, Hanafi fiqh allows a buyer or seller to stipulate an option for a third party. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the ruling and the reasoning behind it, highlighting the use of istihsan to override strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State the ruling from the matn: if a buyer stipulates an option for a third party, it is valid. The contract is sahih (valid) and the third party can accept or cancel.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
2
Contrast with Zufar's qiyas
Understand that Zufar (a Hanafi student) said it invalidates the contract by qiyas. The analogy: option is like price – it must belong to a contracting party. So stipulating it for a non-party is like stipulating price on a non-buyer, which would void the contract.
This is the strict qiyas (qiyas jali).
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Learn the istihsan reasoning: the option is first given to the contracting party, then the party deputizes the third party. Thus the option is still attached to the contract via the party.
Deputyship is a recognized legal concept in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze consequences when multiple parties act
If the buyer, seller, and third party each act (accept or cancel), the earlier action prevails. If simultaneous, cancellation takes precedence because it creates a prohibition.
This shows the hierarchical effect of the option.
5
Apply the rule to ambiguous stipulations
If the stipulation is ambiguous (e.g., option in one of two slaves without specification), the condition is invalid. The sale contract remains valid (the condition is void but not essential).
The ruling depends on specification to avoid gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شرط المشتري الخيار لغيره صح، فأي أجاز أو نقض صح، فإن أجاز أحدهما أو البائع العاقد الشرط عندنا البيع الشرط عندنا البيع ونقض الآخر، فالأسبق أحق، وإن كانا معاً فالفسخ، ولو باع عبدين على أنه البيع منهما الإجازة والفسخ بالخيار في أحدهما، إن فصل وعيّن صح، وإلا لا. أي أحد العبدين ثمن كل واحد منهما العبد الذي فيه الخيار شخص بألف درهم مثلا المشتري: والتقييد بالمشتري اتفاقي؛ لأنه قال في "السراجية والكافي": لو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار لغيره صح. صح: أي الشرط عندنا استحساناً، وقال زفر: يفسد العقد، وهو القياس؛ لأن الخيار من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغير العاقد، كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري، وجه الاستحسان: أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة العاقد فيقدم له الخيار، ثم يجعل الغير نائبا عنه تصحيحا لتصرفه بطريق الاقتضاء، فيثبت له أولاً، ثم ينوبه الغير فيه عنه. . رمز الحقائق: ١٥/٢] (فتح) فأي أجاز: من المشتري أو البائع أو الغير. (عيني) صح: لأن كلاً منهما يملك التصرف أصالة أو نيابة. رمز الحقائق ١٥/٢] أحدهما أي أحد الاثنين وهما من شرط الخيار من المتعاقدين والغير وهو الأجنبي. (عيني)
And if the buyer stipulates the option for another, it is valid. So whichever [party] accepts or cancels, it is valid. Then if one of them accepts, or the seller, the contracting party with the stipulation according to us, the sale with stipulation according to us, and the other cancels, then the first is more entitled; and if they are simultaneous, then cancellation [prevails]. And if he sells two slaves on condition that he has the option in one of them, if he details and specifies, it is valid; otherwise not. i.e., one of the two slaves, the price of each one of them is the slave in which the option is, a person, e.g., for a thousand dirhams. The buyer: and the restriction to the buyer is by agreement; because it is said in al-Sirajiyah and al-Kafi: If one of the two contracting parties stipulates the option for another, it is valid. Valid: i.e., the condition is valid according to us by istihsan. Zufar said: it invalidates the contract, and that is the qiyas; because the option is part of the contract's requirements, so it is not permissible to stipulate it for a non-contracting party, like stipulating the price upon a non-buyer. The face of istihsan: The option for the non-contracting party is only established by the agency of the contracting party; so the option is given to him first, then the other is made his deputy to validate his disposition by way of conclusion; thus it is established for him first, then the other deputizes for him regarding it. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 15/2] (Fath) So whichever accepts: from the buyer, the seller, or the third party. (Ayni) Valid: because each of them has the authority to dispose either originally or as a deputy. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 15/2] One of them: i.e., one of the two, which are the one who stipulated the option from the contracting parties and the third party who is a stranger. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of stipulating khiyar al-shart for a person who is not a party to the contract. The ruling is that it is valid by istihsan (juristic preference), contrary to Zufar's qiyas which would invalidate the contract. The reasoning: the option is first established for the contracting party, who then delegates it to the third party. Thus, any action by the third party (acceptance or cancellation) is effective. If both the contracting party and the third party act differently, the earlier act prevails; if simultaneous, cancellation takes precedence because it creates a prohibition. This is a nuanced ruling that shows the Hanafi willingness to validate transactions through istihsan over strict analogy.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy for a stronger reason, here to validate the contract.
خيار (khiyār): Option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a buyer stipulates the option of rescission for a third party who is not present at the contract?
A) The contract is void according to all Hanafis
B) The contract is valid by istihsan, and the third party can rescind
C) The option is only valid if the third party is a relative
D) The third party must accept the option within the session

Key Takeaway
Stipulating option for a third party is valid by istihsan because the option is first established for the contracting party and then deputized to the third party.

Conflicting Actions by Option-Holder and Third Party
Intra-Hanafi ruling on conflicting actions by option-holder and deputy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi narrations on conflicting actions (ijaza vs faskh) and apply the rule of precedence (temporal or rescission priority).

Core Idea
Rescission prevails over acceptance when simultaneous; earlier action prevails otherwise.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in sales law (buyu‘) where two parties with conflicting verdicts act at the same time. The Hanafi school offers two narrations—one prioritizing rescission (prohibition), the other prioritizing the original party’s action. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to resolve conflicts of legal rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agents and their actions
Clarify that there are two agents: the original option-holder (usually the buyer) and a third party deputy to whom the option was delegated. The conflicting actions are acceptance (ijaza) and rescission (faskh).
2
Apply the temporal rule first
If the two actions occur at different times, the earlier action is effective and the later is void, regardless of which agent acted first.
This is a general principle: time precedence decides.
3
Handle simultaneous or unknown timing
When actions are simultaneous or their order is unknown, the school applies a different rule: rescission takes priority over acceptance.
This is based on the nature of the actions, not the agents.
4
Understand the reasoning (talil)
Two narrations exist. In one (Abu Yusuf), rescission imposes prohibition on the buyer, acceptance permits; prohibition overrides permissibility. In the other (Muhammad), the original contracting party’s action is stronger because the deputy derives authority from him.
The first reasoning rests on a general principle; the second on a hierarchy of authority.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf’s view, the contract is rescinded. Under Muhammad’s, the contract stands if the original party accepted, or is rescinded if the original rescinded.
The mufta bihi is likely rescission priority, making the contract void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحق بما فعل من المتأخر ؛ لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه أحد، وتصرف الآخر بعده لغو. (عيني) وإن كانا معاً: أي مجتمعين بأن أجاز أحدهما وفسخ الآخر، وخرج الكلامان معاً أو لم يعلم وقتهما. (ط، عيني) فالفسخ أي إذا كان الإجازة والفسخ مجتمعين، أو لم يعلم التاريخ، فالفسخ أحق من الإجازة من أيهما كان في رواية كتاب المأذون، وفي رواية بيوع "المبسوط": تصرف المالك أولى من تصرف النائب نقضاً كان أو إجازة، ووجه أحقية الفسخ ؛ لأن الفسخ يوجب الحرمة على المشتري، والإجازة يوجب الإباحة، والحرمة مقدمة على الإباحة، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف وعند محمد تصرف العاقد أولى؛ لأن الأصل أقوى؛ إذ النائب يستفيد الولاية عنه، فلا يكون معارضاً للأصل. (عيني، زيلعي، مسكين)
He is more entitled to what he did than the latter; because it exists in a time when no one opposes him, and the other's action afterwards is void. (Ayni) And if they are simultaneous: i.e., concurrent, such that one accepts and the other rescinds, and the two utterances come together or their time is unknown. (T. Ayni) Then the rescission: i.e., if acceptance and rescission are simultaneous, or the date is unknown, rescission is more entitled than acceptance, from whichever of them it occurs, in the narration of Kitab al-Ma'dhun, and in the narration of Buyu' of al-Mabsut: the action of the owner is more important than the action of the deputy, be it rescission or acceptance. And the face of rescission's priority is because rescission imposes prohibition upon the buyer, and acceptance imposes permissibility, and prohibition takes precedence over permissibility. This is a narration from Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, the action of the contracting party is more important, because the original is stronger; since the deputy derives authority from him, he cannot oppose the original. (Ayni, Zayla'i, Miskin)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the original option-holder (the contracting party) and the third party to whom the option was delegated act in conflicting ways: one accepts (ratifies) the sale, the other rescinds. The ruling: if the actions occur at different times, the earlier one is effective and the later is void. If they are simultaneous (or timing unknown), the school gives preference to rescission over acceptance. Two narrations: In one (Abu Yusuf's), rescission is preferred because it creates prohibition, which takes precedence over permissibility. In another (Muhammad's), the action of the original contracting party (the owner of the right) is preferred because the deputy derives authority from him and cannot override. This intra-Hanafi dispute shows different principles at play: prohibition vs. original authority.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): Acceptance/ratification of the sale; the act of allowing the contract to stand.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Acceptance prevails
B) Rescission prevails
C) The contract is void automatically
D) The dispute must be settled by court

Key Takeaway
When conflicting actions are simultaneous, rescission takes precedence over acceptance in the Hanafi school.

Selling Two Slaves with Option in One: The Need for Specification
Ruling on validity of selling two items with option in only one, requiring specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scenarios of selling multiple items with an option on one, and apply the Hanafi rule that specification of price and option subject is required for validity.

Core Idea
When option is attached to only one of two items, both the item and its price must be specified, else the sale is invalid.

This lesson examines a common transactional scenario: selling two distinct items (e.g., two slaves) while stipulating an option to rescind the sale regarding only one of them. The Hanafi school requires clear designation of which item carries the option and separation of prices; otherwise, uncertainty invalidates the contract. We will parse the four possible configurations and identify the only valid one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the sale involves two items but the option applies to only one. This creates potential ambiguity in the subject matter and price.
2
Understand the requirement of specification
The Hanafi rule: to avoid jahalah (ignorance), both the specific item with the option and its price must be known. If not, the sale is invalid.
Jahalah that leads to dispute invalidates the contract.
3
List the four scenarios
The text enumerates: (1) both price and option-specified (valid); (2) neither specified; (3) price specified but option not; (4) option specified but price not. The last three are invalid.
These scenarios apply only when items are heterogeneous (e.g., two different slaves).
4
Apply the exception for homogeneous items
If the item is homogeneous (e.g., half of a single slave or a measured commodity), specification of price is not required because the half is not distinguishable and does not cause dispute.
This does not require detailing the price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن فصل وعين فكان الداخل في العقد غير الذي فيه الخيار، فما لم يكن ذلك الداخل معلوماً، وثمنه معلوماً، لا يجوز؛ إذ جهالة المبيع أو الثمن تفسد البيع، ولن يكونا معلومين إلا بالتفصيل والتعيين. صح: أي البيع؛ لأن الذي فيه الخيار كالخارج عن العقد فكان الداخل فيه غيره. وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يفصل الثمن ولم يعين من فيه الخيار لا يصح البيع، فالمسألة أربعة أنواع: الأول: أنه فصل ثمن كل واحد وعين محل الخيار، وهذا الذي ذكر في المتن حكمه الثاني: أنه لم يفصل ولم يعين. الثالث: أنه فصل ولم يعين الرابع أنه عين و لم يفصل، فحكم هذه الصور الثلاث أنه لا يصح البيع؛ لجهالة المبيع والثمن أو أحدهما، ولو اشترى كيلياً أو وزنياً أو عبداً واحداً على أن البائع بالخيار في نصفه جاز، فصل الثمن أو لا؛ لأن النصف من الشيء الواحد لا يتفاوت ولا فرق بين أن يكون الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. (عيني، فتح)
If he details and specifies, then what enters the contract is other than that which has the option. As long as that which enters is not known, and its price is not known, it is not permissible; because ignorance of the sold item or the price invalidates the sale, and they will only be known by detailing and specifying. Valid: i.e., the sale; because that which has the option is as if it is outside the contract, so the one entering it is another. Otherwise no: i.e., if he does not detail the price and does not specify which has the option, the sale is not valid. So the matter has four types: First: he details the price of each and specifies the place of the option; this is what is mentioned in the text, its ruling [is valid]. Second: he does not detail and does not specify. Third: he details but does not specify. Fourth: he specifies but does not detail. The ruling of these three forms is that the sale is not valid, due to ignorance of the sold item and the price or one of them. And if he purchases a measured or weighed item or a single slave on condition that the seller has the option in half of it, it is valid, whether he details the price or not; because half of a single thing does not vary, and there is no difference whether the option is for the seller or the buyer. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage deals with a sale where two slaves (or items) are sold together, but the option of rescission (khiyar al-shart) is stipulated only for one of them. The ruling: the sale is valid only if the buyer (or seller) specifies which item carries the option and separately states the price for each item. Without such specification, the sale is invalid due to uncertainty in the subject matter or price. The text enumerates four scenarios, only one of which is valid: when both the price details and the designated item are clearly specified. However, if the item is homogeneous (like half of a single slave or a measured commodity), specification of price is not required because the half is not distinguishable. This shows the Hanafi principle that ambiguity that leads to dispute invalidates a contract, but if the ambiguity is negligible, it is tolerated.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahālah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the subject matter or price that invalidates the sale.
خيار (khiyār): Option to annul or confirm a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
For a sale of two distinct items with an option on only one, both the specific item and its price must be known; otherwise, the contract is void.

Option for a Non-Contracting Party and Simultaneous Exercise
Ruling on stipulating option for a third party and simultaneous exercise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating option for a third party and explain the rule for simultaneous exercise of option, including the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Option for a third party is valid by istihsan; simultaneous exercise prioritizes rescission.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses two important issues: the validity of stipulating an option for someone who is not a party to the contract, and how to resolve when multiple parties exercise their options simultaneously. The Hanafi school, departing from Zufar's strict qiyas, validates such a stipulation through istihsan, treating the third party as a deputy. For simultaneous exercise, the school prioritizes rescission over confirmation. Understanding these rulings is essential for correctly applying khiyar al-shart in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues
Read the passage and note that it covers two distinct problems: (1) stipulating option for a non-contracting party, and (2) simultaneous exercise of option by multiple parties.
The passage transitions from the first issue to the second with 'fa'in kana ma'an' (if they are together).
2
Analyze the first issue: validity of option for a third party
State the Hanafi ruling: it is valid (sahih) by istihsan. Identify the opposing view of Zufar, who follows qiyas and says it invalidates the contract.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar but his view is not mufta bihi.
3
Understand the proof: qiyas vs. istihsan
Zufar's qiyas: option is a requisite of the contract, so cannot be for a non-contracting party (like stipulating price on a non-buyer). Hanafi istihsan: option is first for the contracting party, then the third party acts as deputy. This validates the stipulation.
Istihsan is a secondary source that departs from strict analogy for a more suitable outcome.
4
Examine the second issue: simultaneous exercise
If multiple parties (buyer, seller, third party) exercise option at the same time or timing is unknown, the ruling is that rescission prevails over confirmation.
The basis is that rescission imposes prohibition (hurma), and prohibition takes precedence over permission (ibaha).
5
Distinguish intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on priority
Note two narrations: one gives priority to rescission, another gives priority to the owner's action. Abu Yusuf favors the owner; Muhammad favors the contracting party. The mufta bihi is that rescission is more entitled.
The text adopts the view that rescission is more entitled, based on the principle of prohibition over permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شرط المشتري الخيار لغيره صح، فأي أجاز أو نقض صح، فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر، فالأسبق أحق، وإن كانا معاً فالفسخ. صح: أي الشرط عندنا استحساناً، وقال زفر: يفسد العقد، وهو القياس؛ لأن الخيار من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغير العاقد، كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري، وجه الاستحسان: أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة العاقد فيقدم له الخيار، ثم يجعل الغير نائبا عنه تصحيحا لتصرفه بطريق الاقتضاء، فيثبت له أولاً، ثم ينوبه الغير فيه عنه. فأي أجاز: من المشتري أو البائع أو الغير. صح: لأن كلاً منهما يملك التصرف أصالة أو نيابة. وإن كانا معاً: أي مجتمعين بأن أجاز أحدهما وفسخ الآخر، وخرج الكلامان معاً أو لم يعلم وقتهما. فالفسخ أي إذا كان الإجازة والفسخ مجتمعين، أو لم يعلم التاريخ، فالفسخ أحق من الإجازة من أيهما كان في رواية كتاب المأذون، وفي رواية بيوع "المبسوط": تصرف المالك أولى من تصرف النائب نقضاً كان أو إجازة، ووجه أحقية الفسخ ؛ لأن الفسخ يوجب الحرمة على المشتري، والإجازة يوجب الإباحة، والحرمة مقدمة على الإباحة، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف وعند محمد تصرف العاقد أولى؛ لأن الأصل أقوى؛ إذ النائب يستفيد الولاية عنه، فلا يكون معارضاً للأصل.
And if the buyer stipulates the option for another, it is valid. So whoever exercises the option (by confirming or rescinding) it is valid. Then if one of them confirms and the other rescinds, the earlier is more entitled. And if both are simultaneous, then rescission [prevails]. 'Valid' means the stipulation is valid according to us by istihsan. Zufar said it invalidates the contract, and that is qiyas, because the option is a requisite of the contract so stipulating it for a non-contracting party is not permissible, like stipulating the price on one who is not the buyer. The basis of istihsan: the option for a non-contracting party is not established except by deputyship of the contracting party, so the option is first established for the contracting party, then the other acts as his deputy in it to validate his action by implication. So it is first established for the contracting party, then the other deputizes for him. 'So whoever exercises by confirming' means from the buyer, seller, or third party. 'Valid' because each of them has the right to dispose as principal or deputy. 'And if they are together' meaning both together, such that one confirms and the other rescinds, and both statements come out together or the timing is unknown. 'Then rescission' meaning if confirmation and rescission are simultaneous, or the history is unknown, then rescission is more entitled than confirmation from whomever it comes, according to the narration of Kitab al-Ma'dhun. In the narration of Buyu' al-Mabsut, the disposition of the owner is more entitled than the disposition of the deputy, whether it be rescission or confirmation. The basis for the priority of rescission is that rescission imposes prohibition on the buyer, while confirmation permits, and prohibition takes precedence over permission. This is a narration from Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, the disposition of the contracting party takes precedence because the origin is stronger, since the deputy derives authority from him, so he does not oppose the origin.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Khiyar al-Shart. It addresses two issues: (1) stipulating option for a non-contracting party, and (2) simultaneous exercise of option. The Hanafi position (based on istihsan) is that stipulating option for a non-contracting party is valid, contrary to Zufar who follows qiyas against it. The reasoning is that the option is first established for the contracting party, then the third party acts as his deputy, so the contract is validated. For simultaneous exercise, the relied-upon position (as per the text) is that rescission prevails over confirmation because rescission creates prohibition, which takes precedence over permission. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to Abu Yusuf, the owner's action (whether rescission or confirmation) takes precedence; according to Muhammad, the contracting party's action (being the principal) takes priority. The text adopts the view that rescission is more entitled in case of simultaneous action.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option stipulated by one or both contracting parties within a specified period to confirm or rescind the sale.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Stipulating option for a third party is valid by istihsan; if exercised simultaneously, rescission prevails.

Sale of Two Slaves with Option in One
Ruling on specifying which slave is subject to option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for validity of a sale involving an option in one of two items and apply the ruling to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A sale of two slaves with option in one is valid only if both the price of each and which slave is subject to option are specified.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding a sale where the buyer has an option in one of two items. The key principle is that any uncertainty (jahalah) regarding the sold object or price invalidates the contract. The author enumerates four possible scenarios, only one of which is valid, and provides an exception for a single item sold with option in half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'If he sells two slaves on condition that he has the option in one of them, if he specifies and determines it is valid, otherwise not.' The ruling is conditional on specification.
The condition applies to both price and which slave is subject to the option.
2
Understand the reason for the condition
The commentary explains that the slave subject to option is treated as outside the contract; the actual sold object is the other slave. That slave and its price must be known, otherwise jahalah invalidates the sale.
Jahalah of either the sold object or price makes a sale fasid (corrupt) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Enumerate the four possible scenarios
The passage lists four forms: (1) both price and subject specified – valid; (2) neither specified – invalid; (3) price specified but subject not – invalid; (4) subject specified but price not – invalid.
Only scenario (1) meets the condition.
4
Analyze the exception for a single item
If the sale involves a single commodity (e.g., one slave) and the seller has an option in half of it, the sale is valid even without specifying price, because half of a single thing is uniform and does not cause dispute.
This exception applies only to a single item, not to two separate items.
5
Apply the ruling to new examples
Now test your understanding by considering similar cases: e.g., buying two cars with option in one, or buying a bag of rice with option in half.
Use the four-scenario framework to determine validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو باع عبدين على أنه بالخيار في أحدهما، إن فصل وعيّن صح، وإلا لا. أي أحد العبدين ثمن كل واحد منهما العبد الذي فيه الخيار شخص المشتري: والتقييد بالمشتري اتفاقي؛ لأنه قال في "السراجية والكافي": لو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار لغيره صح. إن فصل وعين فكان الداخل في العقد غير الذي فيه الخيار، فما لم يكن ذلك الداخل معلوماً، وثمنه معلوماً، لا يجوز؛ إذ جهالة المبيع أو الثمن تفسد البيع، ولن يكونا معلومين إلا بالتفصيل والتعيين. صح: أي البيع؛ لأن الذي فيه الخيار كالخارج عن العقد فكان الداخل فيه غيره. وإلا لا: أي وإن لم يفصل الثمن ولم يعين من فيه الخيار لا يصح البيع، فالمسألة أربعة أنواع: الأول: أنه فصل ثمن كل واحد وعين محل الخيار، وهذا الذي ذكر في المتن حكمه الثاني: أنه لم يفصل ولم يعين. الثالث: أنه فصل ولم يعين الرابع أنه عين و لم يفصل، فحكم هذه الصور الثلاث أنه لا يصح البيع؛ لجهالة المبيع والثمن أو أحدهما، ولو اشترى كيلياً أو وزنياً أو عبداً واحداً على أن البائع بالخيار في نصفه جاز، فصل الثمن أو لا؛ لأن النصف من الشيء الواحد لا يتفاوت ولا فرق بين أن يكون الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري.
And if he sells two slaves on the condition that he has the option in one of them, if he specifies and determines it is valid, otherwise not. That is, one of the two slaves and the price of each one, the slave in which there is the option specifically, the buyer. The restriction to the buyer is agreed upon, because he said in al-Sirajiyya and al-Kafi: If one of the two contracting parties stipulates the option for another, it is valid. If he specifies and determines, then the one included in the contract is other than the one in which there is the option. As long as that included one is not known and its price not known, it is not permissible, because ignorance of the sold object or price invalidates the sale, and they will only be known by specification and determination. 'Valid' means the sale is valid, because the one with the option is like outside the contract, so the one included is other than it. 'Otherwise not' means if he does not specify the price and does not determine the one with the option, the sale is not valid. So the issue is of four types: first, he specifies the price of each and determines the place of the option; this is the one mentioned in the text, its rule. Second, he does not specify and does not determine. Third, he specifies but does not determine. Fourth, he determines but does not specify. The rule for these three forms is that the sale is not valid due to ignorance of the sold object and price or one of them. And if he buys a commodity measured by capacity or weight or a single slave on the condition that the seller has the option in half of it, it is permissible, whether he specifies the price or not, because half of a single thing does not differ, and there is no difference whether the option is for the seller or buyer.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It explains the sale of two slaves where the buyer has an option in one. For the sale to be valid, the buyer must specify which slave is subject to the option and state the price of each. Otherwise, ignorance (jahalah) renders the sale invalid. The commentary enumerates four scenarios: (1) both price and subject specified (valid), (2) neither specified (invalid), (3) price specified but not subject (invalid), (4) subject specified but not price (invalid). There is an exception: if a single item is sold with option in half, specification is not required because half of a single thing is uniform and no dispute arises.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance about the sold object or price that leads to invalidity.
فصل وعين (fassala wa 'ayyana): To specify the price and determine the subject of the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the sale of two slaves with an option in one valid?
A) When the buyer has the option in both.
B) When the price and which slave is subject to option are specified.
C) When the seller has the option.
D) When the slaves are sold separately.

Key Takeaway
In a sale of two items with an option in one, both the price and the specific item subject to the option must be clearly stated, otherwise jahalah invalidates the contract.

Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Scope and Validity
Ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin and its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin, identify its limits (number of items and type of goods), and explain the istihsan-based proof against the qiyas-based objection.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid up to three items in qimiyyat, but not four, due to istihsan.

In this passage, the Hanafi school presents its ruling on the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), which allows a buyer to select one item from a set after the contract. The text clarifies the scope: it is valid only for qimiyyat (fungibles) and only for less than four items. The reasoning relies on istihsan (equitable preference) over qiyas, addressing the objection of jahalah (ignorance).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khiyar al-ta'yin. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) under certain conditions.
2
Locate the scope conditions
The text specifies two conditions: the goods must be qimiyyat (not mithliyyat), and the number of items must be less than four (i.e., two or three).
3
Trace the dalil (istihsan)
The Hanafi proof is istihsan: the ignorance (jahalah) does not lead to dispute because the buyer has the choice and the need is satisfied with three items (good, medium, poor).
This overrides the default qiyas that would invalidate due to jahalah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufar and al-Shafi'i disallow khiyar al-ta'yin entirely, based on qiyas: jahalah in the object invalidates the sale.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because istihsan is preferred over qiyas when there is a strong reason (here, delegation to buyer and fulfillment of need).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح خيار التعيين للمشتري في القيميات لا في المثليات. (ط، عيني)] بأن أحد العبدين أو أحد الثوبين يبيع على أن يأخذ المشتري أيهما شاء بتعيينه، أو يبيع أحد العبيد الثلاثة أو أحد الأثواب الثلاثة أو نحوها على أن يأخذ المشتري واحداً منها بتعيينه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦/٢] فيما دون الأربعة : أي يجوز خيار التعيين في الثلاثة أو الاثنين فلا يجوز ذلك في الأربعة من العبيد أو الثياب أو نحوهما. فإن قيل: في هذا البيع مع خيار التعيين جهالة المبيع وهو يمنع جواز البيع. قلنا: خيار التعيين في معنى خيار الشرط، والجهالة التي فيه لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأن الأمور مفوض إلى المشتري فيختار أيها شاء ويرد الباقي، فلا يمنع الجواز، غير أن الحاجة تندفع بالثلاثة؛ لوجود الجيد والوسط والردي، فلا حاجة إلى الأربعة، حتى لو باع أحد الأثواب الأربعة على أن يأخذ واحداً منها لا يجوز، وهو القياس أيضاً فيما دون الأربعة، ولكن جوزنا فيما دون الأربعة؛ لما ذكرنا. وقال زفر والشافعي: لا يجوز في الكل؛ لجهالة المبيع كما هو القياس وجه الاستحسان أن هذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لتعيين من له الخيار فلا تمنع الجواز رمز الحقائق: ١٦/٢]
And the option of specification is valid for the buyer in fungibles (qimiyyat), not in non-fungibles (mithliyyat). That is, one of two slaves or one of two garments is sold on the condition that the buyer takes whichever he wishes by specification, or one of three slaves or three garments or similar, on the condition that the buyer takes one of them by specification. 'In less than four' meaning the option of specification is permissible in three or two, but not in four slaves or garments or similar. For if it is said: In this sale with the option of specification there is ignorance of the sold object, which prevents validity. We say: The option of specification is in the sense of the stipulated option, and the ignorance in it does not lead to dispute, because the matter is delegated to the buyer, so he chooses whichever he wishes and returns the rest, so it does not prevent validity. However, the need is fulfilled with three, because there is good, medium, and inferior, so there is no need for four. Even if he sells one of four garments on the condition that he takes one of them, it is not permissible. And it (qiyas) would also require impermissibility in less than four, but we permitted in less than four for what we mentioned. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible in all, due to ignorance of the sold object, as qiyas dictates. The basis of istihsan is that this ignorance does not lead to dispute because of the specification by the one who has the option, so it does not prevent validity.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) allows the buyer to choose from among a set of items (like slaves or garments) after the contract. It is valid for up to three items, but not four. The reason is that three items cover the range of quality (good, medium, poor), so need is satisfied; four would introduce excessive ignorance. The text also restricts this option to qimiyyat (fungibles) and not mithliyyat (non-fungibles). The Hanafi position relies on istihsan, arguing that the ignorance here does not lead to dispute because the buyer has the choice. Zufar and al-Shafi'i reject it entirely based on qiyas (impermissibility due to jahalah). The Hanafi school responds that jahalah here is tolerable.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option for the buyer to choose one from a specified set of items.
قيميات (qimiyyat): Fungible goods that are valued by weight, measure, or count.

Joint Purchasers with Option: Dispute on Unilateral Rescission
Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Joint Option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on unilateral rescission by a joint purchaser, explain each side's reasoning, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) including its extension to the options of defect and sight.

Core Idea
One joint purchaser cannot unilaterally rescind without harming the seller.

When two people buy an item together with a stipulated option for both, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises: can one of them rescind his share without the other's consent? Abu Hanifa strictly prohibits it, while his two chief disciples allow it. Their reasoning touches on the very purpose of the option, the nature of joint ownership, and the harm to the seller. This disagreement also extends to other options, such as the option of defect and the option of sight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Two persons jointly buy an item with the express condition that both have the option (khiyar). One of them declares satisfaction (rida) and the other wishes to rescind. Can he do so alone?
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that one cannot unilaterally rescind; both must act together. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that each may rescind his share independently.
The text attributes the Sahibayn's view to 'al-thalathah' (the three), likely including Zufar.
3
Analyse the reasoning (dalil) of each side
Abu Hanifa: the option is for both collectively, not individually; unilateral return harms the seller because the item would be returned with the defect of partnership ('ayb al-shirkah). The Sahibayn: the option is prescribed to remove disadvantage (ghabn); each buyer needs to protect himself, and forcing him to accept a confirmed sale he dislikes is unjust compulsion.
Note the difference in emphasis: collective right vs. individual protection.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the Sahibayn, the contract is rescinded only for the rescinding party's share; the other's share remains valid. Under Abu Hanifa, the rescission is invalid and the contract binds both.
This affects subsequent rights and obligations regarding the item.
5
Extend the dispute to other options
The text states that the same disagreement applies to khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) and khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) when there are two joint purchasers.
This shows the principle's generality within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشتريا على أنهما بالخيار، فرضي أحدهما لا يرده الآخر، وله أن يرده حتى ينفسخ العقد في نصيبه؛ لأنه لو لم يملك فسخه كان إلزاماً عليه لا وفيه إبطال لما ثبت من حقه؛ لأن الخيار شرع لدفع الغبن، وكل واحد منهما محتاج إلى دفعه عن نفسه، وكل من الإجازة والفسخ حق له، فلو بطل بإبطال الآخر خياره لم يحصل مقصوده، وبه قالت الثلاثة. وله: أن المشروط خيارهما لا خيار كل واحد منهما على الانفراد، فلا ينفرد أحدهما في الرد؛ لأن حق الرد يثبت لهما على وجه لا يتضرر به البائع، وفي رد أحدهما ضرر بالبائع؛ إذ المبيع خرج عن ملكه غير معيب بعيب الشركة فلو رده أحدهما لرده معيبا بالشركة؛ إذ هي عيب في الأعيان؛ لأنه لا يتمكن من الانتفاع به إلا بطريق المهايأة، وليس من ضرورة إثبات الخيار لهما الرضاء برد أحدهما وعلى هذا الخلاف خيار العيب وخيار الرؤية.
And if two persons buy (something) on the condition that both have the option, and one is satisfied, the other cannot return it. They have the right to return it so the contract is rescinded regarding his share. Because if he did not have the power to rescind, it would be a compulsion upon him without his consent, and that would nullify his right. Because the option was prescribed to remove disadvantage, and each of them needs to remove it from himself. And both confirmation and rescission are his rights. So if the other's invalidation of his option would not achieve his objective. And this is what the three (imams) said. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument: the stipulation is for the option of both, not the option of each individually. So one of them cannot act alone in returning, because the right of return is established for them in a way that does not harm the seller. And in one returning, there is harm to the seller, because the sold item left his property in a condition free from the defect of partnership, so if one returns it, he would return it with the defect of partnership, since partnership is a defect in the items, because the other cannot benefit from it except by rotation (muhaya'ah). And it is not from the necessity of establishing the option for them that they be pleased with one's return. And on this difference is based (the rules of) option for defect and option of sight.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. When two persons jointly buy an item with the stipulation that both have the option, Abu Hanifa holds that one of them cannot unilaterally rescind his share; both must agree. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that each can rescind his share independently. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the option is for both together, not individually; unilateral rescission harms the seller because the item would be returned with the defect of partnership. The disciples argue that the option is for each to protect himself from disadvantage, and forcing him to accept the other's confirmation would be an imposition. This difference also applies to the option of defect and option of sight.

Key Terms
عيب الشركة ('ayb al-shirkah): The defect resulting from partnership in ownership, which lowers the item's value because co-owners cannot fully benefit without a rotation agreement.
مهايأة (muhaya'ah): Rotation or division of use among co-owners to prevent dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does one joint purchaser's unilateral rescission harm the seller?
A) The seller loses profit on the sale.
B) The item would be returned with the defect of partnership ('ayb al-shirkah).
C) The seller must refund the entire price.
D) The option period is extended.

Key Takeaway
When two persons buy jointly with a stipulated option, Abu Hanifa prohibits unilateral rescission to protect the seller from the defect of partnership, while the Sahibayn allow it to protect each buyer from compulsion.

Sale Conditioned on a Specific Skill: Khiyar al-Wasf
Ruling on sale conditioned on a specific skill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a slave is bought with a condition of a specific skill, and identify the buyer's option if the skill is absent.

Core Idea
If the condition of a specific skill is not met, the buyer has the option to rescind.

In Hanafi sales law, a contract may be conditioned on a particular description. When a slave is bought with the condition that he is a baker or scribe, the buyer is protected if that description is false. This lesson explains the ruling and highlights the buyer's right of option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its fulfillment
Determine what skill was specified (e.g., baker, scribe) and check if the slave possesses it to the extent that the name applies.
The condition must be specific and testable.
2
Determine the option when condition is not met
If the slave lacks the skill to the required degree, the buyer has the option (khiyar al-wasf) to cancel the sale or keep it.
The contract remains valid; the option is a remedy.
3
Understand the buyer's statement in disputes
If the seller claims the slave forgot the skill, the buyer's statement is accepted without proof.
This protects the buyer from dishonesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عبدا على أنه خباز أو كاتب، وكان بخلافه، وشرط صحة العقد أن يقدر العبد على الكتابة والخبز قدر ما يطلق عليه اسم الكاتب والخباز، وإن كان لا يحسن هذا المقدار فله الخيار، وإن قال البائع: كان يحسن ذلك لكنه نسي عندك فالقول للمشتري مطلقا. وكان بخلافه: أي بخلاف ما ذكر وصفه بأن كان غير خباز وغير كاتب.
And if he buys a slave on the condition that he is a baker or scribe, and he is contrary to that, (the buyer has the option). The condition for the validity of the contract is that the slave is capable of writing and baking to the extent that the name of scribe and baker applies to him. If he is not proficient to this extent, then he has the option. And if the seller says: He was proficient in that but forgot while with you, then the statement of the buyer is accepted absolutely. 'And he is contrary to that' meaning contrary to the described description, that he is not a baker and not a scribe.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. A sale conditioned on a specific skill (like baking or writing) gives the buyer an option if the slave lacks that skill. The skill must be present to a degree that the title applies. If there is a dispute about the skill, the buyer's word is taken. This protects the buyer from deception.

Key Terms
خيار الوصف (khiyar al-wasf): Option due to a missed condition or description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Validity and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin and explain why it is valid for up to three items using the principle of istihsan.

Core Idea
The buyer's exclusive right to choose prevents jahalah from invalidating the sale—Hanafi istihsan overrides strict qiyas.

This lesson examines the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), a special type of khiyar al-shart. The Hanafi school permits it for sets of two or three items, while Zufar and al-Shafi'i reject it entirely. The underlying debate centres on whether the jahalah (uncertainty) in the sale object is fatal. We will follow the Hanafi reasoning based on istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the ruling as given in the text: khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for sets of two or three items, but not for four or more.
Text says: 'فيما دون الأربعة' (for less than four).
2
Recognize the opposing view
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that khiyar al-ta'yin is invalid in all cases due to jahalah in the object.
Based on strict qiyas.
3
Analyse the opposing proof
The opponents apply qiyas: any jahalah (ignorance) in the subject matter invalidates a sale, so khiyar al-ta'yin is void.
Qiyas is the default method.
4
Understand the Hanafi response using istihsan
The Hanafis argue that the jahalah in khiyar al-ta'yin does not lead to dispute because the buyer alone has the right to choose; thus istihsan (juristic preference) overrides qiyas.
See the justification: 'لتعيين من له الخيار' (because the one who has the option is specified).
5
Determine the practical consequence
Hanafis permit such sales for up to three items; opponents prohibit them entirely. This difference affects real transactions.
Thamarah al-khilaf: the ruling changes based on madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب خيار الشرط
وصح خيار التعيين للمشتري في القيميات لا في المثليات. (ط، عيني)] بأن أحد العبدين أو أحد الثوبين يبيع على أن يأخذ المشتري أيهما شاء بتعيينه، أو يبيع أحد العبيد الثلاثة أو أحد الأثواب الثلاثة أو نحوها على أن يأخذ المشتري واحداً منها بتعيينه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦/٢]
فيما دون الأربعة : أي يجوز خيار التعيين في الثلاثة أو الاثنين فلا يجوز ذلك في الأربعة من العبيد أو الثياب أو نحوهما. فإن قيل: في هذا البيع مع خيار التعيين جهالة المبيع وهو يمنع جواز البيع. قلنا: خيار التعيين في معنى خيار الشرط، والجهالة التي فيه لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأن الأمور مفوض إلى المشتري فيختار أيها شاء ويرد الباقي، فلا يمنع الجواز، غير أن الحاجة تندفع بالثلاثة؛ لوجود الجيد والوسط والردي، فلا حاجة إلى الأربعة، حتى لو باع أحد الأثواب الأربعة على أن يأخذ واحداً منها لا يجوز، وهو القياس أيضاً فيما دون الأربعة، ولكن جوزنا فيما دون الأربعة؛ لما ذكرنا.
وقال زفر والشافعي: لا يجوز في الكل؛ لجهالة المبيع كما هو القياس وجه الاستحسان أن هذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لتعيين من له الخيار فلا تمنع الجواز رمز الحقائق: ١٦/٢] (فتح، عناية)
Chapter of Option of Stipulation. And the option of specification is valid for the buyer in fungible goods (qimiyyat) not in non-fungibles (mithliyyat). (T., 'Ayni)] That he sells one of two slaves or one of two garments on condition that the buyer takes whichever he wishes by his specification, or he sells one of three slaves or one of three garments or the like on condition that the buyer takes one of them by his specification. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 16/2] For less than four: that is, the option of specification is permissible in three or two, but it is not permissible in four slaves or garments or the like. For if it is said: In this sale with the option of specification there is ignorance of the sold object and that prevents the permissibility of the sale. We say: The option of specification is in the meaning of the option of stipulation, and the ignorance in it does not lead to dispute because the matter is delegated to the buyer; he chooses whichever he wishes and returns the rest, so it does not prevent permissibility. However, the need is fulfilled by three due to the existence of good, medium, and bad, so there is no need for four. So if he sold one of four garments on condition that he takes one of them, it is not permissible. And this is also the analogy for less than four, but we permitted it for less than four for the reason we mentioned. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible at all due to ignorance of the sold object as per the analogy. And the justification of istihsan is that this ignorance does not lead to dispute because the one who has the option is specified, so it does not prevent permissibility. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 16/2) (Fath, 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage discusses the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) in sales. It is a type of khiyar al-shart where the buyer has the right to choose one item from a limited set. The Hanafi position is that this option is valid for sets of two or three items but not for four. The reason is that while there is some ignorance (jahalah) about which item will be taken, this ignorance does not lead to dispute because the choice is entirely in the buyer's hands. However, the need for such an option is fulfilled with three items (good, medium, bad), so four is unnecessary. The passage then presents the objection from Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who argue that any such ignorance invalidates the sale, using strict analogy (qiyas). The Hanafi response relies on istihsan (juristic preference): because the buyer's sole discretion prevents conflict, the sale is valid. This is a classic example of Hanafi istihsan overriding qiyas.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option of specification: the buyer's right to choose one specific item from a set of two or three similar items within a specified time.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or ambiguity in the contract subject matter that could lead to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school permit khiyar al-ta'yin for sets of three items but not four?
A) Because the buyers' need is fulfilled with three options (good, medium, bad).
B) Because the Prophet (s) forbade selling four items with an option.
C) Because analogy (qiyas) requires it to be invalid for four.
D) Because the sale becomes a contract of gambling with four items.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits khiyar al-ta'yin for up to three items because the jahalah is tolerated under istihsan, as the buyer's exclusive right to choose prevents disputes.

Joint Buyers and Option: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint buyers' option to rescind

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on joint buyers' options and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When two buyers jointly purchase with an option, one's acceptance binds the other per Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn allow each to rescind his share.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding joint purchasers who both have an option. When one buyer drops his option and accepts the sale, can the other still rescind? Abu Hanifa says no, because the right is joint and rescission would harm the seller. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes, because each has an individual right to protect against deception. Understanding this disagreement is key to applying the Hanafi school's preferred view in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two persons jointly purchase an item with a stipulated option for both. One drops his option and accepts the sale. The question: can the other still rescind?
The option is shared (khiyar al-shirkah).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the other cannot rescind. His evidence: The stipulation is for the option of both, not individually. Returning the item would cause a partnership defect, harming the seller.
The seller would receive a co-owned item, which is defective because co-ownership limits use.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the other can rescind his share. Their evidence: The option is legislated to prevent deception; each buyer has an individual right. Dropping by one does not bind the other.
They analogize to khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'yah.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, if one accepts, the sale is binding on both. Under the Sahibayn, the second can rescind his half, and the sale remains valid only for the first buyer's half.
This affects the seller: partial return vs. full return.
5
Note the cross-madhhab alignment
The three other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree with the Sahibayn. Within Hanafism, Abu Hanifa's view is the mufta bihi.
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, as it better protects the seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشتريا على أنهما بالخيار، فرضي أحدهما بأن أسقط خياره، لا يرده الآخر، وقالا له أن يرده حتى ينفسخ العقد في نصيبه؛ لأنه لو لم يملك فسخه كان إلزاماً عليه وفيه إبطال لما ثبت من حقه؛ لأن الخيار شرع لدفع الغبن، وكل واحد منهما محتاج إلى دفعه عن نفسه، وكل من الإجازة والفسخ حق له، فلو بطل بإبطال الآخر خياره لم يحصل مقصوده، وبه قالت الثلاثة. وله: أن المشروط خيارهما لا خيار كل واحد منهما على الانفراد، فلا ينفرد أحدهما في الرد؛ لأن حق الرد يثبت لهما على وجه لا يتضرر به البائع، وفي رد أحدهما ضرر بالبائع؛ إذ المبيع خرج عن ملكه غير معيب بعيب الشركة فلو رده أحدهما لرده معيبا بالشركة؛ إذ هي عيب في الأعيان؛ لأنه لا يتمكن من الانتفاع به إلا بطريق المهايأة، وليس من ضرورة إثبات الخيار لهما الرضا برد أحدهما. وعلى هذا الخلاف خيار العيب وخيار الرؤية. (عيني، فتح)
And if two purchased together on condition that they both have the option, and one of them is pleased by dropping his option, the other cannot return (rescind). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He can return so that the contract is rescinded regarding his share, because if he does not have the power to rescind it, it would be binding on him and that would invalidate what is established as his right. For the option is legislated to prevent deception, and each of them needs to prevent it from himself, and both acceptance and rescission are his rights. So if his option becomes void by the other's cancellation, his objective is not achieved. And the three (the other schools) also said this. And for him (Abu Hanifa): The stipulation is for the option of both of them, not the option of each individually. So one of them cannot unilaterally rescind, because the right to rescind is established for them in such a way that the seller is not harmed. In the rescission by one of them there is harm to the seller, because the sold item left his ownership without the defect of partnership. So if one of them returns it, he returns it defective with partnership, for partnership is a defect in the goods since one cannot benefit from it except through division (muhaya'ah). And it is not necessary from the establishment of the option for them to consent to rescission by one. And upon this disagreement is the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) and the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah). (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding joint purchasers who both have an option. The scenario: two people buy an item together with the condition that they both have the option to confirm or rescind. If one of them drops his option and agrees to the sale, can the other still rescind? According to Abu Hanifa, the other cannot rescind because the option is joint; the right to rescind is not individual. If one party rescinds alone, the seller would be harmed because the item would be returned with a partnership defect (since now it is co-owned), which reduces its value. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the other can rescind his share because the option is an individual right to protect against deception, and the other's dropping it does not bind him. They compare this to khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'yah where similar rulings apply. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is more protective of the seller's rights and consistent with the joint nature of the contract.

Key Terms
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option of the buyer to rescind or seek compensation due to a defect in the purchased item.
المهايأة (al-muhaya'ah): A division of benefit or time-sharing between co-owners to avoid mutual interference.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option to rescind a sale after seeing an item purchased unseen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why can one joint buyer not rescind after the other has accepted?
A) Because the buyer dropped his option, so the sale is binding.
B) Because returning the item would cause a partnership defect harming the seller.
C) Because the option is only valid for three days.
D) Because the seller has already received the full payment.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when two persons jointly purchase with a joint option, one buyer's acceptance binds the other, and the latter cannot rescind unilaterally.

Khiyar al-Wasf: Option for Missing Stipulated Skill in Slave Sale
Ruling on khiyar al-wasf for missing skill in slave sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-wasf when a slave is bought with a described skill, identify the minimal standard for the skill, and apply the option when the skill is missing.

Core Idea
A missing described skill gives the buyer an option, but only if the slave lacks the minimal ability to be called by that skill name.

When you buy something based on a described quality, what happens if that quality is missing? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses exactly that scenario in the context of a slave sale. The Hanafi school treats a missing stipulated skill as a defect, giving the buyer a right to return (khiyar al-wasf). But the key is the minimal threshold: the slave must be capable enough to bear the name of the skill. Let's unpack the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying a slave with a stipulated skill (e.g., baker or scribe). The ruling is that the sale is valid (sahih) if the slave has the minimal skill, but the buyer has an option (khiyar) if the skill is missing or insufficient.
This is a case of khiyar al-wasf (option for missing description).
2
Locate the condition for validity
The text states a condition for the validity of the contract: the slave must be capable of the skill to the extent that the name (e.g., 'scribe' or 'baker') can be applied. This is the minimal standard.
It is not about perfection; just enough to be called by that name.
3
Determine when the option arises
If the slave does not possess even that minimal ability, the buyer has the option to return the slave or seek compensation. The option arises because the stipulated quality (sifah) is missing.
The option is a khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) in Hanafi law, as the missing skill is considered a defect.
4
Analyze the seller's claim of forgetfulness
If the seller claims that the slave was skilled but forgot (at the time of delivery), the buyer's word is taken (on oath). The seller's claim is essentially an admission that the skill is absent now, so the buyer's claim prevails.
This is a procedural rule: the buyer's denial of having witnessed the skill is accepted.
5
Apply the minimal standard test
Given a scenario, determine whether the slave meets the minimal standard. For example, a slave who can write only a few letters is not a scribe; a slave who can bake only one type of bread poorly might still be called a baker.
The test is: can the slave be reasonably described by that skill name in common usage?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عبدا على أنه خباز أو كاتب، وكان بخلافه، فله الخيار. وشرط صحة العقد أن يقدر العبد على الكتابة والخبز قدر ما يطلق عليه اسم الكاتب والخباز، وإن كان لا يحسن هذا المقدار فله الخيار. وإن قال البائع: كان يحسن ذلك لكنه نسي عندك فالقول للمشتري مطلقا. (عيني، فتح)
And if one buys a slave on condition that he is a baker or scribe, and he is contrary to that, then he has the option. And the condition for the validity of the contract is that the slave is capable of writing and baking to the extent that the name of scribe and baker can be applied to him. If he does not possess this extent, then he has the option. And if the seller says: He used to be proficient in that but he forgot in your presence, then the word is of the buyer absolutely. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a buyer stipulates a specific skill (like baking or writing) in a slave. If the slave turns out not to possess that skill or possesses it insufficiently, the buyer has khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) due to a missing described quality. The contract is valid only if the slave meets the minimal standard for that skill. If the seller claims the slave was skilled but forgot (a denial of the defect), the buyer's claim is accepted on oath, because the seller is effectively admitting that the skill was absent at the time of delivery.

Key Terms
خيار الوصف (khiyar al-wasf): Option of defect due to missing a described quality (sifah) that was stipulated in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer buys a slave on condition that he is a scribe, and the slave can write only a few letters, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is void because the condition is not met.
B) The buyer has the option to return because the minimal skill is missing.
C) The sale is binding because the slave can write.
D) The buyer must accept the slave and cannot return.

Key Takeaway
When a slave is bought with a described skill, the contract is valid only if the slave has the minimal ability to be called by that skill name; otherwise the buyer has an option to return.

Remedy When Buyer Retains Item with Missing Description
Ruling when buyer retains item despite missing description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi remedy of price reduction when a buyer keeps an item after discovering a missing described quality, and calculate the compensation using the valuation method.

Core Idea
If a described quality is missing and return is impossible, the buyer claims the exact market value difference via appraisal.

This lesson explains the Hanafi rule when a buyer retains an item despite a missing described quality (khiyar al-wasf). The buyer has two options: accept at full price or return. If return is impossible, he is entitled to the difference in market value between the item as described and as it actually is. This remedy ensures fairness without forcing the buyer to suffer a loss or the seller to refund the entire price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Buyer's Two Options
The buyer may either accept the item at the full price (waiving the defect) or return it (rejecting the sale due to the missing description). These are the primary choices.
If the buyer chooses to keep the item, he cannot later demand a partial refund unless return becomes impossible.
2
Determine When Price Reduction Applies
The price reduction remedy (ruju' bi al-nuqsan) applies only when return is impossible, e.g., the item is lost, consumed, or already transferred to a third party.
If return is possible, the buyer must either return or accept; he cannot claim a partial refund.
3
Understand the Valuation Method
The item is appraised twice: once as if it possessed the described quality (e.g., as a scribe) and once as it actually is (without that quality). The difference (al-tafawut) is the compensation.
The appraisal is based on market value at the time of discovery, not at the time of sale.
4
Apply to a New Scenario
Practice by taking a real case: a buyer purchases a car described as having leather seats, but they are fabric. He keeps the car after it is registered. Compute the compensation by obtaining market valuations with and without leather seats.
The buyer must prove the missing description significantly affects value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذه بكل الثمن أو ترك الوصف المرغوب فيه. رجع بالنقصان بأن يقوم كاتباً وغير كاتب، فيرجع بالتفاوت.
He takes it with the full price or leaves the desired description. He recovers the deficiency by evaluating it as a scribe and as a non-scribe, and takes the difference.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage explains the remedy when a buyer retains the item despite a missing described quality. The options are: either accept the item at the full price (i.e., waive the defect) or return it. If return is impossible (e.g., the item is lost or consumed), the buyer claims the difference in value between the item as described and its actual value. This is done through valuation: the item is appraised as if it possessed the described quality and as it actually is, and the buyer receives the difference. This is a standard Hanafi rule for khiyar al-wasf when return is impracticable.

Key Terms
التفاوت (al-tafawut): The difference in value between the item as described and its actual value at the time of defect discovery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer keeps a slave who was described as a scribe but is not, and cannot return the slave, how is compensation calculated?
A) The buyer can demand any amount he wishes.
B) The buyer receives the difference between the price paid and the market value of a non-scribe slave.
C) The buyer receives the difference between the value of the slave as a scribe and as a non-scribe.
D) The buyer gets nothing because he kept the slave.

Key Takeaway
When return is impossible, the buyer's remedy for a missing described quality is the exact difference in market value determined by appraisal of the item with and without the quality.

Valid vs. Invalid Stipulated Descriptions
Principle for valid descriptions in contract conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a valid description from an invalid condition in a sale contract by applying the Hanafi gharar principle.

Core Idea
A stipulation is valid only if it describes a knowable quality without measurement or uncertainty.

Not every description or condition attached to a sale is acceptable. The Hanafi school sets a clear boundary: descriptions that are certain and verifiable are valid; anything that introduces uncertainty (gharar) in quantity or hidden state is an invalid condition that renders the contract void (fasid). This passage from al-ʿAynī’s commentary on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq lays down the rule and illustrates it with concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Locate the principle: any description without gharar is permissible to stipulate; any with gharar is not, unless it is a disclaimer.
The rule is stated clearly at the start of the passage.
2
Distinguish description from condition
Understand that a valid description (sifah) must be a knowable, non-quantitative attribute. A condition (shart) that imposes a quantitative or unknown result introduces gharar and invalidates the contract.
The examples contrast 'halub' (milker) vs. pregnancy or specific milk quantity.
3
Analyze the examples
Work through each example: (1) selling a camel on condition of pregnancy – invalid because pregnancy is uncertain; (2) selling on condition of milking a specific amount – invalid; (3) selling as 'halub' – valid; (4) slave baking specific amount – invalid; (5) slave writing specific amount – invalid.
The reasoning is that quantity is not part of a description (ليست الوصف لا تعلق له في المقدار).
4
Apply the exception
Note the exception: if the stipulation is in the sense of disclaiming existence (البراءة من وجوده), i.e., the seller states that the attribute is not present, the condition is valid.
This allows a seller to guarantee the absence of a defect, for example.
5
Formulate the ruling
Conclude: the contract is fasid (void) if a stipulated condition involves gharar; it remains valid if the stipulation is a genuine description or a disclaimer.
The practical import: a buyer cannot rely on speculative promises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس كل الأوصاف يصح العقد باشتراطها، بل الضابط فيها أن كل وصف لا غرر فيه فاشتراطه جائز، لا ما فيه غرر، إلا أن يكون اشتراطه بمعنى البراءة من وجوده بأن لا يكون مرغوباً فيه. وعلى هذا لو باع ناقة أو شاة على أنها حامل، أو تحلب كذا وكذا أرطالاً، حيث يفسد البيع؛ لأنه ليس من قبيل الوصف، وإنما هو من قبيل الشرط الفاسد؛ إذ لا يعرف الحمل واللبن حقيقة؛ لأنه يحتمل أنه لبن أو دم أو حمل أو انتفاخ، حتى لو شرط أنها حلوب أو لبون لا يفسد؛ لأنه وصف ولو قال: إن العبد يخبز كذا صاعاً، أو يكتب كذا قدراً يفسد؛ لأن الوصف لا تعلق له في المقدار، فلا يكون وصفاً بل شرطا فاسداً، والجارية كالعبد في جميع الأحكام. (عيني، فتح)
And not all descriptions make the contract valid by stipulating them; rather the principle is that any description without gharar, its stipulation is permissible, not one with gharar, unless its stipulation is in the sense of disclaiming its existence, meaning it is not desired. And upon this, if one sells a she-camel or a sheep on condition that it is pregnant, or that it milks so many ratls, then the sale becomes invalid; because it is not of the category of description, but rather of the category of invalid condition, since pregnancy and milk are not known in reality because it could be milk, blood, pregnancy, or swelling. Even if he stipulates that it is a milker (halub) or lactating (labun), it does not invalidate; because it is a description. And if he says: The slave bakes so many sa's, or writes so much, it invalidates; because the description does not relate to quantity, so it is not a description but an invalid condition. And the slave-girl is like the slave in all rulings. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage lays down the Hanafi principle for valid descriptions in contracts. The key is the absence of gharar (uncertainty). A description must be knowable and not speculative. For example, stipulating that a sheep is pregnant or produces a specific quantity of milk is invalid because pregnancy and milk quantity are uncertain (could be false, could be other substances). However, describing it generally as a 'milker' (halub) is acceptable because it refers to a characteristic, not a specific measure. Similarly, stipulating that a slave can bake a specific amount of bread or write a specific number of pages is invalid because quantity is not a stable description; it is a condition that introduces gharar. The general rule: any stipulation that is a true description (sifah) without uncertainty is valid; anything that introduces speculative or quantitative conditions makes the contract fasid (void).

Key Terms
غرر (gharar): Uncertainty or risk in the object or consideration of a contract that leads to potential dispute or fraud.
وصف (waṣf): Description or attribute of the object of sale that is stable, knowable, and not based on quantity or hidden state.
شرط فاسد (sharṭ fāsid): An invalid condition that renders the contract void (fasid) because it introduces gharar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does stipulating that a slave 'bakes a specific number of sa' of bread' invalidate the sale?
A) Because baking bread is not a valid profession.
B) Because quantity is not a stable description and involves gharar.
C) Because the slave may not agree to bake.
D) Because the buyer cannot verify the baking ability.

Key Takeaway
A stipulation in a sale contract is valid only if it describes a known attribute without quantitative uncertainty; otherwise, it is an invalid condition that renders the contract fasid.
